Simdrome
171 products in account
0
538 people found this review helpful
8 people found this review funny 93

Recommended
104.2 hrs on record
Posted: January 3
A Brief Introduction
The year is 2001. The anticipated sequel to the smash hit, Metal Gear Solid, has just been released. Immediately, outrage is sparked and the game becomes the bastard child of the franchise, for one primary reason:

The fans hated Raiden.

It’s been 21 years since then (Insane, right?), and where’s all the hate gone? People actually LIKE Raiden now? Why’s that?
This game is why, and here's why you should definitely get it.

In-Depth Analysis
Gameplay
Platinum Games, famously the creators of Bayonetta and Nier: Automata, are no strangers to fast-paced hack and slash games. In fact, they’re probably the best developers in the genre. When Kojima asked them to make a hack and slash game based in the Metal Gear universe with Raiden as the lead, they delivered in spades.

Gameplay is actually very simple. Unlike Bayonetta and Devil May Cry, where the player is buried in weapon types to switch in and out, MGR gives you a single sword and says “Go nuts kid.” You have light attacks, heavy attacks, and all the combos that gives you. Very easy to pick up, very easy to get into.

What makes the Metal Gear Rising stand out from the pack is its emphasis on parrying enemy attacks and using your high-frequency blade to cut through anything in your way, enemies included. A properly directed light attack in the direction of the enemy deflects their hit, preventing the player from taking what could potentially be crippling damage on higher difficulties. Considering there is no block button, and dodges are slow and unreliable, parrying is the only decent way to avoid taking damage. MGR did it before Sekiro made it cool, although it's not nearly as demanding in the timing as Sekiro was.

Equally, healing items are incredibly scarce, requiring players to utilize MGR's unique combat mechanic of “Zandatsu”. By either stunning or damaging an enemy enough, players can slice them open with blade mode and rip out their fuel cells, refilling his health to full. Knowing the proper time to slice n’ dice and having good precision in your moves is the key to success, and on Revengeance difficulty, it's often the only way to stay alive under the onslaught of enemies thrown at you.


Proper parry timing and precise aim is heavily rewarded, or even potentially mandatory on higher difficulties. 
Community Created Artwork for Steam Artwork
By: Xenos


To further emphasize how beginner-friendly this game is, unlike some hack and slash games that give you no warning and expect you to memorize all enemy attack patterns to dodge, Metal Gear Rising gives you a fair chance to react to what’s coming, leaving it up to the player to respond. Parryable enemy attacks are indicated by a red flash in their eyes, while unblockable attacks (Usually grabs) are indicated by a yellow glow.

The gameplay is fast, engaging, and easy to get the hang of. The bosses also take full advantage of this system to deliver memorable battles that I still hold in high regard to this day.

The only iffy part of the gameplay loop is that, probably due to being a Metal Gear game, Platinum Games included an incredibly minimalist and half-baked stealth system. While Raiden can see enemies through walls, and can “backstab” them, he has no sneaking mechanics, or really any way to hide. At best, it's a way to take out a few enemies before you inevitably get spotted and the massive brawl breaks out. At least there’s not really a penalty for getting spotted, unlike in MGS; you can just chop them in half.

The game also has a high level of replayability. Although the story and setpieces don't change, the rating system pushes players to improve their performance throughout, and every new difficulty level can change the enemies one encounters in each area. On normal, the first fight of the game is just against a handful of soldiers. On Revengeance difficulty, you're immediately thrown against a Gekko mech, along with several dogs.

Story
This is a Metal Gear game. Those that have played the Metal Gear Solid series know what this means. To those that have not: This entire game is both a serious political commentary, and an absolute joke at the same time. The topics can often be very serious, such as terrorism fueling the war economy, creating jobs, and being unpleasantly good for a nation. This is true; World War 2 actually pulled the American economy out of the Great Depression.

But then the next minute, you have a cyborg ninja debating philosophy with a sentient robot dog, Raiden wearing a mariachi band outfit, and most famously, a terrorist declaring that “Memes are the DNA of the soul.”


Metal Gear Rising absolutely revels in how absurd it is at every opportunity, and it's fantastic. 
Community Created Artwork for Steam Artwork
By: Xenos


On the surface, the combination of dead-realism and complete absurdity seems incompatible, but the game owns it by being acutely aware of how crazy it’s being, embracing it, and running wild with it. It’s the same writing logic that propelled Metal Gear Solid into being rated one of the best series of all time.

In the end, it creates an incredibly fun way of discussing genuinely serious topics, though sometimes the absurdity overshadows the horror of what’s happening in the moment.

However, this IS a canon part of the Metal Gear universe, meaning it makes numerous references to the events of the other games. If you haven’t played the other games, you won’t understand what people are saying every now and then, but thankfully the majority of the dialogue is self-contained within Rising, preventing too much confusion. If you’re one of those people that really loves their lore or needs context, I would heavily encourage you to play or watch the Metal Gear Solid series, as they are equally excellent games.

Visuals
The game looks great, plain and simple. The game is somewhat dated by today’s standards, having come out in 2013, so you don’t have to look hard to find some rough edges, unrefined models, and simplistic architecture. It makes up for this with good art and character design making them visually memorable and interesting. MGR especially loves its particle effects, so expect lots of those.


Metal Gear Rising has an excellent sense of cinematography and presentation. 
Community Created Artwork for Steam Artwork
By: Xenos


Audio
Even the biggest detractors of Metal Gear Rising never deny one thing: The music in Rising is AWESOME. The intense electric metal perfectly suits the cybernetic themes of the game, and the boss themes are incredible, both lyrically and musically. “Rules of Nature” was the go-to edgy meme song before “Bury the Light” from DMC5 took its place 6 years later. In fact, you’ve probably heard Rules of Nature at some point if you haven’t been living under a rock since 2013. I still listen to the boss themes when working at my PC.

Technical
GeForce RTX 3050Ti 4GB | Intel i7 | 16GB | Windows 10
Obviously a game from 2013 better run on my specs, but it’s important to note it also ran perfectly fine on my old PC from 2013, which only had a GeForce 840m 2GB and 8 GB of RAM. Unless you’re still using your 2005 Windows XP PC held together with duct tape, you should be able to run this game on good settings with good frames.

A controller is HEAVILY recommended due to the precise omni-directional nature of the game. Keyboard and mouse parrying is so difficult in comparison that MGR was the sole reason I bought my first PC-compatible controller.

Conclusion
Very Highly Recommended
Metal Gear Rising isn’t necessarily a one-of-a-kind experience; you can get the same story from Metal Gear Solid, and the same general gameplay from any hack and slash. However, the combination of the two styles, great sense of visual design, amazing soundtrack, and ease of accessibility make it a worthwhile purchase for any gamer. It can drop down to less than $7 on sale, but it’s worth the full price.

Get it when you can!

Follow our curator page, OCG-Curations, if you like and want to see more reviews like this one.
 

Xenos

NUKExPYRO
170 products in account

786 people found this review helpful
234 people found this review funny 62

Recommended
32.9 hrs on record
Posted: June 14
Senator Armstrong talked about an omelette.

I'm not really American so take this Vietnamese omelette recipe from google

1 chilli
2 spring onions
2 limes
60g smooth peanut butter
1 tsp sugar
1 tsp fish sauce
2 tsp rice vinegar
60ml water
4 British Lion eggs
200g raw king prawns
50g beansprouts
Bunch of mint
Bunch of coriander
Salt
Coconut oil

Start by slicing your chilli, spring onions and cut one of your limes into wedges.
Place all your red chillis in a bowl with your peanut butter, sugar, soy sauce, fish sauce, rice vinegar, the juice from your remaining lime and water. Give it all a good mix until you have a smooth sauce. Set aside until later.
Beat your British Lion eggs in a bowl with 2 tbsp water and a generous pinch of salt.
Heat a large frying pan over a medium-high heat. Add a teaspoon of coconut oil and, once melted, add your prawns. Fry for a minute on one side, then flip over.
Pour your egg mixture into the pan so it forms a thin, even layer. Turn up the heat and cook for a minute, sprinkling in the spring onions as you go.
When the surface of the egg is nearly firm, sprinkle in your bean sprouts and flip your omelette in half so that you have a lovely half moon.
Tip your omelette onto a plate and open up the middle. Fill it with a handful of coriander, mint and your remaining sliced chillis. Serve up with your dipping sauce and enjoy.

Look out for the British Lion mark on your eggs to guarantee that they’ve been produced to the highest standards of food safety. You can find them at your favourite supermarket.

PS. I think this recipe was made by americans so it might not taste good

Recommended
30.0 hrs on record
Posted: June 1
There’s a saying I like: “One sword keeps another in the sheath.”
METAL GEAR RISING: REVENGEANCE is a hack-and-slash action game, contrasting significantly with the franchise’s slower-paced, stealth-focused gameplay. In the high-tech future of 2018, our fellow cyborg, Raiden, must get to the bottom of a conspiracy by causing violence, The Only Thing He Knows.

This is my normal. My nature.
At first glance, it looks about on par with other late-7th console generation games. Serviceable texture work, scenery and shading that’s occasionally on the bland side, but never ugly to look at. Environments are usually littered with destructible items. What visually sets this title apart are the extraordinarily well-done animations and particle effects, which help provide a spectacularly smooth experience, both in cutscenes and during gameplay.

For the PC port quality, trying to play it above 1080p resolution is a little annoying. One needs to use a fan-made patch to trick the game into running at the desired resolution, with the caveat that it causes minor UI corruption, and requires one to change the graphics settings on each boot. Full keyboard rebinding is possible, but a gamepad is recommended. Otherwise, I’m happy to report a steady and stable experience at 1440p 60hz, with a Ryzen 9 3900X, 32GB RAM, GeForce 1070Ti, Windows 10 Pro system.

RULES OF NATURE!

Yes, within the first 10 minutes, you kick the arse of a skyscraper-sized mecha. It only gets better from here. 
A Screenshot of METAL GEAR RISING: REVENGEANCE
By: A Tomato

Get ready for some bang-up electronic rock and metal music to headbang to. The tracks played during boss fights are the highlight of the soundtrack, yet all in-game music features a subtle variable mix that lets the also-impressive vocals kick in or fade out during pivotal moments of combat. Hardly any better music to chop up your foes to.

In fact, there’s nothing amiss in the sound department at all. Rich and appropriately-acted dialogue, with the villains providing all the ham and cheese you can ever ask for. Powerful and sharp sound effects to give excellent feedback on your combat moves and statuses. It’s all just top-notch, really.

All we're sayin' is... GIVE WAR A CHANCE!
Peace doesn’t last long in the world that is now dominated by cyborg-staffed private military contractors. The Prime-Minister of an unnamed African nation, for whom Raiden provides bodyguard protection, is kidnapped and then bloodily murdered by the head of the Winds of Destruction. The loss of an arm barely deters our hero; determined to find and punish the people responsible for the murder, Raiden and his contacts uncover a sinister plot to stir chaos for profits – in the process, unearthing dark truths about himself and his “fight for justice”.

This is a genuinely fun story to follow, of course thanks primarily to the colourful cast of excellent characters. Between the middle of the game and the finale, however, it tends to languish some due to the lack of meaningful conflict or development.

My sword is a tool of justice.
As one of your mission-control characters state, this isn’t a sneaking mission. Beyond token stealth elements, mastery of the combat loop and its mechanics is key to victory. Raiden himself has very few defensive options starting out: only a “ninja run” to deflect bullets while travelling rapidly, and a directional block - which can be upgraded to a powerful riposte if the player times the block just before the enemy’s attack connects. These blocks and ripostes, unfortunately, need precise movement inputs towards the attacking enemy, meaning there are times when Raiden misses the block and gets chopped.

A couple more criticisms about the core gameplay are that the camera is pretty poor and uncooperative. Locking onto enemies helps little when it has a tendency to look away from the action. Also, many controls are unexplained and left for the player to discover by trial-and-error, such as quick-firing sub-weapons.


Yes, there are setpieces with quick-time events, but none ever feel badly done. The action is awesome, and the timings are generous. 
A Screenshot of METAL GEAR RISING: REVENGEANCE
By: A Tomato

Otherwise, that’s really the extent of my gripes with METAL GEAR SOLID: REVENGEANCE. Combat is exceptionally fluid, with lots of varied combos to pull off by stringing sequences of light-and-heavy strikes, on the ground or in the air. Of course, the selling point of the game is Blade Mode. Raiden can temporarily slow down time, angle a precise swing (or fifty) of his blade, and slice apart weakened enemies to instantly kill and have a chance at refilling his own health and energy meters. With dramatic pauses for effect and a sweet “Dead on!” from Raiden, catharsis goes through the roof.

To aid in combat, players can make use of various “sub-weapons” like thrown grenades and rocket launchers, as the only means of ranged utility or offense. Cumbersome to use without proper preparation or the aforementioned quick-firing, but can help turn the tide in your favour when things go poorly.


Not once does it fail to feel satisfying to rip open an enemy and crush their nanopaste unit. 
A Screenshot of METAL GEAR RISING: REVENGEANCE
By: A Tomato

I want… more!
And sweet goodness, the bosses are AWESOME. Beyond testing your knowledge of the game systems like a proper video game boss would (albeit with a difficulty spike or two around the mid-game) – they’re also some of the most memorable individuals to grace my library of games. When the game isn’t throwing a solid variety of fodder and mini-boss enemies your way to hack into a thousand pieces, it’s having you battle single foes on equal terms, usually while grandiose setpieces and kickass music play out. Exploding refinery as a backdrop? That’s only in the first hour, and things only get crazier towards the end!

This is what happens when you bring a tool to a sword fight!
Players earn currency via combat and rank gradings, which can be used to purchase additional abilities and enhancements for Raiden. Word of advice: take the Defensive Offensive ASAP. It's a useful dodge move. You also unlock more items and upgrades as you progress through the story and perform certain feats.

A chunk of extra content can be gathered through the VR Missions. Taking place in abstract environments, players have a variety of tough challenges to complete that encompass basically every major gameplay element on show. Included in the Steam release are some 30 extra VR Missions, but 20 still have to be unlocked by accessing hidden terminals scattered throughout the campaign.

There will be BLOOD! SHED!
The main campaign clocks in at some eight to ten hours in length, on Hard difficulty. Repeat playthroughs are encouraged in order to unlock more weapons, have your skills tested on higher unlockable difficulties, and especially to find more collectibles. Due to space constraints, I’ll just state that there’s a lot to collect.

The PC version also includes a boss-rush mode, should you want to skip all that awesome combat and get straight to awesome 1v1 combat instead. Last but not least, two extra stories can be played, taking you through familiar territory as other major characters from this title. These, in turn, control almost entirely differently, but just as satisfying as Raiden. The DLC campaigns themselves are rather short, at just two to four hours apiece – and the stealthy character’s story drags on at the start – but are overall a great inclusion nonetheless. Thus, full completion can take well over 30 hours to attain – a great deal at the usual price.

But no matter how jagged your path is,
You always come back to the road.
When the dust of battle settles,
The war still rages within…
Supremely satisfying combat, great replayability and awesome presentation elevate METAL GEAR RISING: REVENGEANCE into a superb recommendation for all lightning-fast action players.

Raiden, get to the curator, Tomato’s Bag of Games! Do not miss out on great reviews, this time!
 

A Tomato

Recommended
14.6 hrs on record
Posted: May 16, 2016
Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance is an awesome game. It is a third person action hack and slash game with some epic boss battles. You play as Raiden who is a cyborg ninja/human hybrid. The story begins with Raiden working security detail for the president of an African country, they are attacked by the Desperado (A private military company) and their leader Sundowner kills the president N’mani. You fight numerous bosses. I will avoid spoilers by giving the details of the story here.

Graphics:

The graphics in Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance are pretty good. It doesn’t have the best looking textures but you won’t notice them unless you go really slow. The game is supposed to be played fast and you’re constantly fighting enemies to notice the texture anyways. Game seems to be locked at 60 fps so I wish it went higher. The game is optimized pretty well as I never dipped below 50 in fps throughout the game, even when a lot was going on screen, it ran very smooth. The game features one of the best looking cinematic cut scenes, I don’t usually take many screenshots in games but this game had me take over 600 screenshots throughout the gameplay. Though the cut scenes are locked at 30 fps for some reason, they’re nothing too annoying but it is definitely noticeable.

There’s the usual options in this game like texture filtering, antialiasing, shadow quality, motion blur etc. Graphics menu image can be seen below:


for review purposes 
A Screenshot of METAL GEAR RISING: REVENGEANCE
By: Thugnificent


Sound:

This game features an epic sound track. The voice acting is pretty solid. The game features a fast paced heavy metal/rock soundtrack. Even though I am not a fan of this genre of music I thoroughly enjoyed the music. Basically the music really pumps you up, especially during boss battles, you have that high rush and energy going on with this sort of music.

Gameplay:

The gameplay of this game is amazing and one of the best hack and slash gameplay I’ve ever played. Raiden has a basic blade which he uses to slice up enemies, later down the game you gain additional weapons and even a new blade near the end of the game. Raiden can use light and heavy attacks by left and right clicking respectively. You can create a lot of combos using these attack combinations and even unlock new moves with the in-game currency. There’s a Parry move which can be used to block almost every attack in the game (though some attacks will still hurt Raiden, like the last boss battle’s MG Excelsus form). You have to hit the direction of the enemy and your light attack button at the same time to be able to successfully a parry an enemy attack. When an enemy attacks you they’ll have a red light go off in their eyes and this is your chance to parry. A good practice in parrying is your key to beating this game otherwise some of the bosses will have you raging. Successful parrying of an attack will block the enemies’ attack and an electric current can be seen as visual confirmation of a successful parry. When you’ve nearly killed an enemy you can also go into blade mode and try to hit the red box which prompts up on the enemy, upon successful hit on the box Raiden will rip out the enemy’s heart out and crush it with his bare hands, this will refill both his fuel cell energy bar and health bar. When you’ve almost killed an enemy you may also get a prompt in Japanese to attack in blade mode or a series of quick time event moves. A lot of boss battles will also make use of the QTE’s.

When you fight enemies you gain battle points which can later be spent on new weapons, health and fuel cell upgrades and new moves. New suits can also be bought some of which have different feature such as one of the suits can have Raiden carry more grenades etc. Later down the line Raiden gains “Jack the Ripper” mode which can be activated using the R key. When you’re in ripper mode Raiden will start to glow red and his attacks do much more damage and you can easily kill of even the super cyborg mechs with a few hits. There’s also a Nano paste pickup which basically an add-on which refills your health once the whole bar depletes. Having a few of these before boss battles can also be very handy. Raiden’s health upgrades can go up to 150% and the fuel cell upgrades can add four small additional mini bars.

The weapons/recovery menu could’ve used an upgrade as it’s kind of limited. Every time you want to change a weapon you must go through this weapon menu. This is not too troublesome for the health or main weapon but can be annoying if you switch your sub weapons a lot. Even though PC’s have enough buttons to assign every weapon their own button they still decided to use this dumbed down console version of the menu which is quite painful to use. Menu as seen below:


for review purposes 
A Screenshot of METAL GEAR RISING: REVENGEANCE
By: Thugnificent


Raiden has plenty of abilities such as ninja run which is Raiden running super-fast with his sword out and he blocks bullets with his blade. Basically when someone shoots with guns you can use this to avoid getting hurt. Ninja run will also have Raiden auto jump over obstacles. You can also use this to harass enemies by moving in getting a few hits and then moving away though this method is not as effective as most of the enemies have a lot of HP and can take a long time to kill. There’s a sort of a dodge ability, when you press Z key, Raiden will attack enemy and sort of jump back, it’s not that useful, I mostly used parry throughout the game and found that to be much better. In addition to that Raiden has what is called a blade mode. It basically slows down the game and you can cut up an enemy into many pieces and you can accurately cut up the enemy or objects. When you are in blade mode you can adjust the angle of your blade and make horizontal, vertical or diagonal strikes and at the end of blade mode the enemy/object will be cut exactly in normal time as well. A short gameplay featuring combat, parrying and Ripper mode as well as blade mode can be found below:


Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance short gameplay [60FPS] 
A Video of METAL GEAR RISING: REVENGEANCE
By: Thugnificent
For Steam Review purposes.


Every level has you follow a linear path and a bunch of enemies to kill. Leading up to a boss battle. There’s many types of enemies including military guys with guns and rocket launchers, ninjas with blades, heavy armed cyborgs, even cyborg hounds etc. You can hide in cardboard boxes, metal barrels just like other Metal gear games, which can be hilarious. When enemies detect you, you’ll hear the ah-so-familiar exclamation mark sound from other Metal gear games. You can also get stealth kills and do most missions via stealth as well by sneaking behind enemy and pressing F when the prompt comes up.

I played on normal mode, game is not that difficult, though, the last boss can be pretty hard to beat and frustrating, others were not so hard. The game doesn’t require too much time to beat, you can easily beat the game in less than 8 hours of gameplay in normal mode. VR modes unlocks are hidden throughout the levels and must be activated to unlocked in order to play.

Graphics: 7/10
Sound: 9/10
Gameplay: 10/10
Overall: 9/10

Conclusion:

This game is extremely fun and if you’re a Kojima fan or even a fan of action/hack and slash games, you’ll love this game. Awesome soundtrack which will keep you pumped up during intense boss battles, some of which can last up to 10 minutes. Make your way by slicing up everything that moves or go the stealth way and try to eliminate one enemy at a time. The game features awesome cinematics and an interesting story which will keep you hooked and plenty of Kojima humor. I’ll 100% recommend this game. I really hope more PlatinumGames’ games make it to the PC.

Posted: March 15
If you're looking for a review on this game you've come to the wrong place, but if you're looking for an outstanding pie recipe you've come to the right place.

Ingredients:

1. 6 tablespoons unsalted butter
2. 1/2 cup white sugar
3. 1/2 cup brown sugar
4. 1/4 cup water
5. 1/4 teaspoon cinnamon
6. 1 pinch salt
7. 5 apples - peeled, cored and sliced
8. 1 pastry for double-crust pie

Directions:

1. Preheat oven to 425 degrees F (220 degrees C).
2. Combine butter, white sugar, brown sugar, water, cinnamon, and salt in a saucepan over medium heat. Bring to a boil, remove from heat and set aside.
3. Roll out half the pastry to fit a 9-inch pie plate. Place bottom crust in pie plate; pour in apple slices.
4. Roll out top crust into a 10-inch circle. Cut into 8 (1-inch) wide strips with a sharp paring knife or pastry wheel. Weave the pastry strips, one at a time, into a lattice pattern. Fold the ends of the lattice strips under the edge of the bottom crust and crimp to seal.
5. Pour butter-sugar mixture over top of pie, coating the lattice, and allowing any remaining sauce to drizzle through the crust.
6. Bake in the preheated oven for 15 minutes. Reduce heat to 350 degrees F (175 degrees C), and bake until the crust is golden brown, the caramel on the top crust is set, and the apple filling is bubbling, 35 to 40 more minutes. Allow to cool completely before slicing.

How to make the MOTHER OF ALL OMELETTES: (inspired by Red3Speed)

1.
Use two or three eggs per omelette. Beat the eggs lightly with a fork.
Melt the butter over medium-low heat, and keep the temperature low and when cooking the eggs so the bottom doesn’t get too brown or overcooked.

2.
Let the eggs sit for a minute, then use a heatproof silicone spatula to gently lift the cooked eggs from the edges of the pan. Tilt the pan to allow the uncooked eggs to flow to the edge of the pan.

3.
Fold the omelette in half. Slide it onto a plate with the help of a silicone spatula.

Ego
21 products in account

1,108 people found this review helpful 0

Recommended
11.9 hrs on record
Posted: January 9, 2014
Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance is a collaborative effort between Platinum Games and Hideo Kojima.

What we’re left with is an extremely fast-paced hack and slash title set in the Metal Gear universe. Solid Snake fans will immediately be disappointed as you once again play as the ninja cyborg; Raiden.

The highlights of the game are the fast-paced combat, the stunning visuals, and the ridiculous boss fights. MGSRR does a great job with their combat system which is designed to keep you on the offensive while you chain together parries and attacks without the over-reliance on dodging.

The game also adds a “slice anywhere” mechanic which allows you to cut wherever you aim. This essentially allows you to cut enemies and objects in the environment into a million pieces. This really doesn’t add anything significant to the gameplay but it’s still quite a bit of fun.

The graphics, visuals, and environments are great. It’s a treat to watch the explosions and chaos unfold around you as you move from one varied area to the next. Unfortunately, the game is fairly linear and doesn’t allow for much room for exploration as you’re constantly hit with frustrating blue boundaries.

The game features an over the top story with plenty of humor mixed in. It’s entertaining but don’t expect the same level of depth as other Metal Gear Games.

The inclusion of VR missions, where you have to complete simple objectives in a virtual reality training program add a bit more content. The main game is very short however, clocking in at around 5 hours. Granted it’s a fun-filled 5 hours as the game features some of the best boss fights on the market.

A few extra things to note:
A controller is recommended for the game.
This is a console port. It does look better on the PC than the Xbox 360 and PS3 but it is capped at 1920 x 1080 resolution. This means if you're using a 2560 x 1440 resolution monitor, you won't be able to run it at that resolution, you'll have to downscale to 1080p.

For a more in-depth review, here’s a video I made:


Analog Reviews: Metal Gear Rising Revengeance 
A Video of METAL GEAR RISING: REVENGEANCE
By: [AReV]Nomed
Our Analog Review of Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance by Senior Editor Nathan. Metal Gear Rising Revengeance is a collaborative effort between Platinum Games (Original Devil May Cry creators) and Hideo Kojima.


Pros:
Amazing gameplay
Stunning Visuals
Fantastic Boss Fights
Can cut things up into a million pieces

Cons:
Short Length and a lack of content in general
Linear with a lack of exploration
Story isn't up to par with other Metal Gear games.


If you enjoyed this review, feel free to follow me as a Steam Curator: http://store.steampowered.com/curator/4886473/

I've cut a car into a thousand pieces in 3 seconds. 11/10 GOTY!

Just kidding of course. This stupid and pathetic type of reviews are killing me. If you can't write a few decent sentences about a game - why bother ? But enough about it, let's talk about the game.

Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance is the hack-and-slash spinoff of the Metal Gear series, and a damn good one. Absolutely no Metal Gear knowledge or experience is required. You get to play as Raiden - a half-human, half-cyborg ninja through a 10-15 hour single-player campaign. After completing it you also get two bonus mini campaigns where you can play as Jetstream Sam & Blade Wolf, each of them having their own features. But that's not all. There are also a lot of VR missions to unlock in the main story as well as in the secondary ones, which you can play later at any time.

MGR:R has a good story accompanied by a great soundtrack. Although not exactly my type of music (metal rock), it fits entirely the game's atmosphere. The game is locked at 60 fps, but that's fine with me. It has a great art design and good visuals. Still, the best part is the combat and the gameplay itself. There are some stealth features available which were imported from the Metal Gear series, like barrels and boxes you can use to hide from enemies or sneak through undetected, but don't get fooled by that, this is not a stealth game by far, on the contrary - it's a "go on rampage" type. There are many different types of enemies, and you can cut each one of them in as many pieces as you want and also finish them with some nice looking finishing moves, including stealing the life source from their cyborg equipments. MGR: Revengeance is also very rewarding. There is a in-game currency which you can earn and use it to unlock new skills, well designed weapons which can also be improved, as well as extending your health and energy bar, and acquiring new costumes for your character, including my favourite - the Mariachi one. For some reason, slaughtering cyborgs wearing a Sombrero felt a lot better ^_^ Btw, I almost forgot to mention the amazing boss fights. I won't describe anything about it so i don't have to include any spoilers, but they are quite memorable. You'll see that for yourself.

I recommend Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance without any doubt, and i assure you it is worth every penny from its full price. If you're into hack-and-slash or fast-paced games - this would be one of the best choices you could make.

Recommended
21.2 hrs on record
Posted: January 15, 2014
If you like games like Ninja Gaiden, Devil May Cry, Bayonetta, or God of War, you'll be right at home with this game.

Most gamers will probably know what the Metal Gear series is all about before going into this game. If you count yourself among these people, then try to forget what you know about Metal Gear. This game stands alongside other games in the franchise, but it is worlds apart in gameplay and tone. Metal Gear Solid games are primarily about stealth and story. Revengeance is about action, plain and simple.

The gameplay is phenomenal. Platinum has a gift with the Hack N' Slash genre and it shows with Rising. The combat is fluid and challenging while still being fun and accessible. The parry mechanic feature heavily in the game and while it may take some time to master for some, it's incredibly satisfying when you pull off a perfect parry and counter-attack an enemy for extra damage. There are certain fights that require you to have a decent handle of the move as well, and if you don't the game will help you out by beating it into you.

What's truly revolutionary is the parry/dodge mechanic in the game. Rather than having a dedicated block button, Revengeance makes it a forward+attack input, which maintains offensive momentum. You need to parry every attack coming at you, but the game's window is generous, allowing for a lot of wiggle room until you nail down your timing. And once you nail down that timing? You get perfect parries with counterattacks that lead into Zandatsu (slowdown cutting mechanic where you can steal energy cores).

Even if you don't get the combat, or you're an action game novice, the game features a number of different difficulty levels to tailor the experience to what is most comfortable for you as a player.

The story is filled with its own levels of abrudity, but features a memorable cast and set of bosses. The bosses... Oh, the bosses. They're some of the best of this entire generation- meticulously crafted and exhilarating to fight.

This game is seriously good, one of the best I've played. If you're a Metal Gear fan (who isn't busy whining that Snake isn't playable), a hack and slash fan, or someone who just likes fun, check this out. You won't be disappointed.

A fast action game with solid game play music and decent story with the metal gear charm where stealth isn't the dominant game play but will be required at higher-level difficulties. This is a side story game where you play as the bad ass ninja Raiden, After a short intro on the execution of a country's minister by Desperado, you'll be taken forward in time to the point where Raiden will go after the armed coup that Desperatdo started to find out what is going on and what the private service companies are up to.
The Gameplay is pure action, Slicing, cutting, ripping, and cutting things your way, There will be side weapons you'll earn as you defeat bosses in the game with precise cuts with the katana. the game play slashing and slicing don't as just one-button presses, depending on where you aim and how you slice you can chop your enemies up to pieces. You'll want to chop their hands and certain places to take their spine so you can take it in as health when you need it and of course when this happens, free form blade mode time slows down enough for you to aim at your enemies on those precision cuts. Later in the game, you'll be able to do ripper mode where you'll go into overdrive. Sub weapons and extra items you can carry and use in this game, which are literally almost useless at times except for specific enemies and at higher end play.

The control for this game is better off played with a controller over a mouse and keyboard which was much easier personally to me for this type of game, though that is a preference, there will be intense fights where the key is to actually be on point for the attacks otherwise you're going to get yourself killed.
The soundtrack is absolutely rocking in this game, the music is big time adrenaline pumping, and you'll love it along with the funny voice overs. Ah yes the famous metal gear voice overs. Basically if you don't know what I am talking about you been missing out. It is hilariously bad at times but still well done for being bad, and that's what makes the game great.
Once you beat multiple hard modes, there is an even harder mode where you are required to sneak and kill your enemies and to challenge your skills to the limit, don't believe that the stealth is the best part of this game though and only at the highest level difficulty will you be forced to use it.

Fasut
540 products in account

116 people found this review helpful
11 people found this review funny 0

Recommended
78.1 hrs on record
Posted: April 19, 2015
In the first installment of the "Rising" series of the Metal Gear franchise, cyborg super-soldier Raiden is dispatched on a mission against a private military company held responsible for acts of terrorism. The truth happens to be more than that in the end.

The famous (or infamous) spin-off from the original Metal Gear Solid series, Revengeance brings a gameplay shift from the usual stealth third person shooter into an action-packed hack-and-slash sword fighting game. With Raiden's main weapon being the high-frequency blade, the player is put to engage several enemies that vary from regular sword-fighters, to rocket-launching cyborg soldiers, to huge assault mechs.

Gameplay

As mentioned above, Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance has mainly action gameplay. Implementing the occasional use of one of its main game mechanics, the "Zandatsu" (lit. 'cut and take'), used to slice off foes and extract energy units to replenish your own. Stealth is present in the game, as you can sneak past or stealth-kill a number of enemies, but at little quantity given the action genre of the game.

Sided with Zandatsu comes the parrying game mechanic, which will give you an extra edge (no pun intended) on combat given its often prompt to deal finishing Zandatsu attacks upon a 'perfect' parry. It's also the only method of defense that doesn't involve dodging in the game, making it your incentive to master it.
(Note: it is HIGHLY RECOMMENDED you have a controller of some sort to play this game, as mouse and keyboard gameplay is extremely complicated.)

Combat in the game feels pressing and complicated at higher difficulty levels, giving an extra challenge on levels Hard and above. In addition, there is the presence of some quick-time events, as well as boss fights of the game which usually feel absolutely riveting, from fast-paced cyborg vs. cyborg combat to slicing off pieces of humongous mechs.

The only down side is an arena-style limited area during fights.

Plot

The story begins in a recently-enforced African country, introducing Raiden as now a member of private military corporation 'Maverick Security Consulting Inc.'. During a guard duty task, President N'mani is hijacked and killed by military contractors of Desperado Enforcement LLC. Months later, Raiden is deployed in tasks to investigate terrorist activities found out to be backed by Desperado. It happens though, it's more than just power and money at play as Raiden uncovers a bigger scheme.

The story is over-the-top and characters are -on the least- quirky. Not that it's a bad thing, and it gives the game its distinction from Metal Gear Solid franchise. Just get ready for cyborg ninja fights and explosions.

Soundtrack

Lead composer Jamie Christopherson did an amazing job with the soundtrack of Revengeance, both in the less-famous ambient music and in the better-known vocal tracks, perfectly fitting the situations and characters involved in the longest time. It sets the mood and gives the finishing touch of the game, being also one of the highlights of the game.

Bugs

Little if any that I know of or could see.

Overall

Albeit opinions vary, Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance surely does good work in the fighting/action game genre, even if breaking somewhat from the known Metal Gear Solid formula.Revengeance being my first Metal Gear game, in my opinion it's a game worth a play and should be taken in consideration.
 

♆Major✠Dirtymcnasty❝.❛
205 products in account
10

Recommended
134.2 hrs on record
Posted: September 9, 2020
Information

Title: Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance
Developer(s): PlatinumGames
Publisher(s): Konami Digital Entertainment
Genre(s): Action, hack and slash
Game Engine: PlatinumGames game engine
Release Date: 9 Jan, 2014
Mode(s): Single-player

Review

Hideo Kojima had a vision of transfiguring a solid tactical espionage title into a rising lightning bolt action game; from here, Metal Gear Solid Rising was born. It began as a slow-paced, hack-and-slash game following the route of its predecessors, combining swordsmanship with spectral gameplay. By utilizing the Fox Engine, the cardinal objective was to create a game that swings between being stealthy and action-oriented. To focus on other projects, Kojima made a wrong call by leaving the game's development process to his team.

Without his guidance, Hideo's team was lost, since they were struggling to balance the preconceived slashing mechanics with the level design of the game. Luckily, a company that is well-known for engineering fast-paced games handled the project, hence saving it from its demise. Abandoning the Fox Engine, PlatinumGames utilized its own game engine to integrate the Metal Gear universe into a trailblazing, brief game. The resultant of all this is Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance, an excellent game that had a rocky development, yet surpassed our expectations with honors.

It's laughable to picture a casual player booting up the game, thinking it would have mercy on a new soul, and then his first fight is with a 20 meters tall versatile UG. The main story is weaved to be very engaging thanks to the nonplus twists that radically alter the plot from being ordinary to being pre-eminent. The overall character design of MGR is its mystic quartz. Raiden is made into a badass by amplifying his cybernetical, charismatic, and psychological attributes. Bosses, who sporadically appear in the ordinary game's events, will be the glimmering stars of the show thanks to their eccentric mien and distinctive battles.

Fitting soundtracks that correlate with each one of them play a crucial role in their appeal. The boss battles are the pinnacles where MGR's combat style will glister. They are programmed using the concept of the RNG algorithm, which means that memorizing their attack patterns won't be very helpful here. I will never forget this battle with the fierce demagogue; it will be a memory in my heart when we both said, "This is the greatest fight of my life!" concomitantly while an epic song was playing in the background.

The camera has issues that dreadfully impact controlling Raiden in combat. The lack of a FOV dilating option in the graphics menu makes matters even worse. It's tormenting to strive for the no damage bonus in a ranked battle when a cheapass enemy can easily strike you with a charged attack which was commenced off camera. The best way to circumvent this problem in boss fights is to lock-on the boss so for the camera to be focused on him. Sadly, this option is useless in battles that have multiple enemies attacking you.

What makes the story's content so chirpy is that it demonstrates serious matters and does something out of the box to imply that it doesn't take itself that seriously. The dialogue within the copious codec conversations has adequate data that renders NPCs' personalities quite well. The intervention of amusing moments in solemnly themed sceneries is exhibited wonderfully; this supplements the premium quality of the sceneries that is a vital property for reinvigorating the story aspect and its elucidation.

Being a Platinum game, the prime focus of MGR is encouraging direct encounters with enemies. Furtive gameplay is notably dispirited by substandard stealth mechanics and lesser BP points. There are 3 weapon categories in the game: primary blades, unique weapons acquired from fallen bosses, and secondary weapons. All the previously mentioned weapons are quite useful in the specific circumstances they are designed for. A judicious combination of attacks orchestrated from them can be devastating, hence ending a battle that could've lasted 8 minutes in 20 seconds, especially in the highest difficulty.

In MGR, QTEs are adroitly concatenated within combat. Jacked animations executed while a first-rate soundtrack is playing in the background are guaranteed to initiate some goosebumps. QTEs in Revengeance mode are the ultimate win, as they do a significant amount of damage in boss confrontations. Blade mode, the transmuting feature that MGS:R was going to be based on, puts the player into slow-motion where he can perform a 斬奪, which is a special technique used by Raiden, to extract electrolytes from enemies to replenish his fuel cells and health.

The controls in this game are well-suited for a controller; they are vexing when using a keyboard and mouse. Exempli Gratia: when a f*cking mastiff grabs Raiden's ass around, the player is prompt to rotate the controller's analog in circles to evade the grab; to match this using a keyboard, the player must press W, A, S, D simultaneously in supersonic speed to cope with the responses of an analog rotating—it's very strenuous to do so. Using the evade technique with a keyboard is quite hard in certain fights when the direction of the evade is essential in a fight.

Let's not ignore the elephant in the room, shall we? The VR missions in MGR stands for violating rectum missions. They are programmed for the sole purpose of infuriating the player. After achieving the highest score in the total of 50 VR missions available, I felt ashamed for the amount of time I've wasted on these cheap challenges. They came too close to ruining the entire game for me. I won't cover all of their issues, but I will mention a few of them. First of all, their map design is nauseating. They take place in a bland yellow environment that lacks anything interesting.

The prime concept of these missions is trial and error. The player must try a challenge like 25 to 100 times based on his luck for the one time when all the positive factors align together to make setting the highest score achievable. Let's take VR mission 17 for example: in this mission, the player must destroy waves of aggressive enemies using sub-weapons. For starters, the rocket launcher's mechanics are slow as hell, and it's mainly useful to take down choppers. The player can use the quickfire technique, but sadly, he is in no control of where the shots are fired, as it's up to the rocket launcher to choose for him.

DL-VR mission 27 wins the prize for being the Brobdingnagian pain in the ass. It's very hard and has a flawed design. The player is at the mercy of the merciless AI. The problem with this map is that at the final round, one of the 4 fenrirs will comet suicide by jumping off the map or exploding, which shatters the chance for a 斬奪, hence rendering all the hard effort to get to this exasperating round pointless. The overall performance of the game is decent. I didn't encounter any problems, lags, or crashes. The maximum resolution of the game is 1920x1080, and aspect ratios other than 16:9 are anamorphic. Also, the game doesn't support 4K resolution properly.

> Verdict:

To Hideo Kojima: you never cease to amaze!
To PlatinumGames: keep up the adrenaline doses!
To Senator Armstrong: you made this game enthralling. I will never forget you.
To VR missions designers: I hope you all go bankrupt as soon as possible.

Looks like I finally found the best video game character of all time, all hail ✧ JETSTREAM SAM ✧

Alright first off I wanna say that this game doesn't do a very good job of explaining how parrying works so i will quote a helpful statement which i found - "you have to rapidly use analog & atk button AT THE SAME TIME, meaning after a parry you'll have to press analog & atk button again to re-activate parry, holding the analog and press atk button alone won't activate parry." Mikey
411 products in account
3
101 people found this review helpful
2 people found this review funny 9

Recommended
33.0 hrs on record
Posted: January 28, 2021
-Gameplay-
🔲 My 90 year old grandma could play it
🔲 Easy
☑️ Normal
🔲 Hard
🔲 "Dark Souls"

On most difficulties, this game is a pretty fair game, even on some of the harder difficulties. The game gives you plenty of upgrade choices for you to be able to prepare yourself for higher difficulty runs. However, the hardest difficulty in the game, Revengeance difficulty, will NOT hold back. It is a good test of your strength of how far you've come. If you've prepared well for it, then you can put up a good fight with the skills you've learned along the way, but the final boss will still make you struggle a fair amount before he lets you pass him on this difficulty.
DLC: The first of these two DLCs however is HARD. You will struggle on even some of the easier difficulties.


-Graphics-
🔲 "MS Paint"
🔲 Bad
🔲 Meh
🔲 Graphics don't matter in this game
☑️ Good
🔲 Beautiful
🔲 Masterpiece

This game is a 2013 game, so of course you shouldn't be expecting anything too fancy. However, it's aged pretty well, despite the couple of pre-rendered cutscenes this game has have a JARRING contrast to the gameplay part, but doesn't diminish anything.


-Story-
🔲 This game has no story
🔲 Like playing "Temple Runners" for the story
🔲 It's there for the people who want it
🔲 Well written
☑️ Epic story

This is a Metal Gear game, a series that is known heavily for its deep and meaningful stories that at times even predict the future in classic Kojima fashion. However, this game did not have the series creator, Hideo Kojima, apart of its creation. Despite this, this game hits all the marks perfectly for a Metal Gear game, and so well in fact, you probably wouldn't know he wasn't apart of it. It's not one of the more deeper games of the series (while still having some depth), but it most certainly has strong meaning to it, and yes, great future predictions that have aged VERY well in funny ways.


-Music-
🔲 Bad
🔲 Not special
🔲 Good
☑️ Beautiful

This game's music is absolutely phenomenal. The rock is great and fuels the gameplay perfectly with how much the music flows through you. Don't believe me? You can turn the music completely off in the settings. Try playing any boss fight without music and it'll hurt and be an extremely missed aspect with how much it works in tandem with the game.


-Length-
🔲 Very short (0 - 3 hours)
☑️ Short (3 - 15 hours)
🔲 Average (15 - 50 hours)
🔲 Long (50 - 90 hours)
🔲 Extremely long (90 - 110 hours)
🔲 No ending

The length. This game can be completed in about 5-6 hours depending how fast you get the controls down and what difficulty you're playing on. This is one of those games where its biggest problem really is that it is just too short. You'll want more, yet because of how Konami has been after this game's release, it isn't very likely that we'll see a sequel, even though the series creator, Hideo Kojima, praised Platinum's work on this game, and the person who was behind this game is still working at Konami.
DLC: There are two DLCs, but they are basically just two semi-longer missions for you to play afterwords.


-Fun-
🔲 I'd rather watch paint dry
🔲 Hard to enjoy
🔲 Repetitive
🔲 Actually pretty amusing
☑️ Ride of your life

This game really is a joyride of an experience. Despite this game being apart of a notoriously "where should I start" series, this game actually takes place after the whole Metal Gear Solid saga. Therefore, while you would of course get more enjoyment out of this game with knowledge on the series, this can be enjoyed even as outsider to the series. Think of the Metal Gear Solid saga as Marvel's Infinity Saga and this game is the start of what's next to come.
Once you learn how to play well and unlock more and more upgrades, you will just get more joy going on and on with the strength you can feel your character get when playing.


-Price-
🔲 Free
🔲 Underpriced
🔲 Perfect price
☑️ Could be cheaper
🔲 Overpriced
🔲 Complete waste of money

$30 is not a bad price for this game, especially with how many positive points this game has. However, the length of it really is the game's most jarring flaw. If you can find this on sale for $20, don't hesitate.


-Replayability-
🔲 It's a one - time experience
🔲 Only for achievements
🔲 If you wait a few months / years
🔲 Definitely
☑️ Infinitely replayable

There are so many upgrades in this game, some helpful, some just fun outfits to wear for a different experience. You have a decent amount of collectibles and even extra mini-missions you can always go back to in order to unlock more extra things. And even once you get all the collectibles and missions, it's still so fun to just go through the story again (and this time, probably a beast with all your upgrades) just for the fun of it.


-Requirements-
☑️ You can run it on a microwave
🔲 Average
🔲 High end
🔲 "NASA" computer

This is a 2013 game for the Xbox 360 and PS3, so of course, it's not very hard to play this. However, this game plays a little better with a controller. It's not bad on keyboard and mouse, but because of how fluid some game movements are, a controller is just the king of course at times.


-Worth buying?-
🔲 No
☑️ Wait for sale
🔲 Yes


Final Notes: Let this meme be passed down.

Recommended
85.5 hrs on record
Posted: November 25, 2017
The game does a fantastic job at capturing the overall tone of Metal Gear all the while creating a whole new experience of action-based gameplay that can stand confidently on its own. While the port does suffer from a couple of issues, there is nothing that can't be fixed quite easily.

It's worth mentioning that the QTE's are actually used properly, which is pretty rare in most games. The soundtrack could also very well be one of the best OSTs in action games that I've ever heard.

Fans of other hack 'n' slash games will feel right at home on this one, even if Metal Gear isn't something you're familiar with or cared about previously.

Packed with tons of unlockables and hidden collectables, the game demands multiple playthroughs in order to fully gain access to all of the abilities. While previous entries of the series rely heavily on stealth, it is beneficial on certain parts to use the silent approach but it is never forced.

Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance is an incredible action game that can be enjoyed by Metal Gear fans and non-fans on equal ground.

Pros :

- Quite fun regular gameplay. Simple, easy and nice.

- amazing boss fights,

- GOD TIER soundtrack ( but only for bosses, the rest is meh )

- My most favorite and memorable final boss of any game.

- Though slightly rushed and unpolished, free DLC is awesome, different characters with different playstyles is neat, despite Blade Wolf's combat moveset being rather crappy.

- Cool special boss weapons?

- Cringy, often edgy but fun dialogue. I dont know who the fu.ck wrote the final boss dialogue, but he deserved a raise for sure.

- Extremely quotable. [s] SHOW ME A GOOD TIME, JACK! [/s]

- Better than Kojima's. Thanks, Platinumgames.

Cons :

- Sometimes a bit crappy against multiple enemies

- Camera is horrible

- Sensivity is broken for me on keyboard, but its tolerable. Makes blade mode a pain in the ass but still completely usable. Do yourself a favor and play it on a controller.

- The hardest difficulty, despite being named after the game, is a joke, because it buffs your parry damage ridiculously high. As if parrying wasnt already OP.

- Dodge move which is a near must - have is an optional upgrade which is never explained to the player (???). Buy Offensive Defense as soon as possible.



Despite all the cons, the game is a solid 9/10 imo. I see why many people wouldn't like it, but i personally loved it.

Recommended
22.2 hrs on record
Posted: April 30, 2016
Don’t **** with this game!

Metal Gear Rising marks Platnium's first PC release and the first, major spinoff of the MGS games in awhile. How does it compare to Platnium's past works?

Pros:
Visceral and Fun Combat!
A good scoring system that incentivizes good performance in the game’s levels.
Campy but sometimes ridiculous plot!
Absolutely killer soundtrack.
Fairly decent port.

Nitpicks:
The DLC included in the full game are either cheat items or half-assed bonus missions. Disappointing, to say the least.
VR Missions aren’t fun to play.

Cons:
Strange Game Design flaws such as a awkward camera and the lack of projectiles can hurt the experience.
Cinematic cutscenes look incredibly janky due to being 30fps pre-rendered cutscenes.

The Review

Metal Gear Rising surprisingly takes place after the events of MGS4, where instead of stealthing your way through problems, you’ll be hacking and slashing almost everything as Raiden. So what does Platinum bring to the table?

Of course, as always seen in Platinum Games, highly visceral combat completely steals the show. Platinum’s trademark brawling combat is visibly present in the game, but it takes a lesser focus on combos in favor of the game’s “Blade Mode”, which allows you to (when the enemy is stunned) hack and slash at enemies in almost any angle. So while you can still slash your enemies with simple X/Y button combos, you’ll be performing much better if you take advantage of your normal attacks to than attack vulnerable enemies with precision. As a result, your normal sword slashes definitely won’t feel as powerful as you’d want them to be, but that’s OK because those weak attacks will open up to insane finishers that really drive up the action of the game. It’s a good system that encourages and rewards players to play as best as possible as they can in every single combat scenario, as getting high ranks/slashing certain body parts will net you bonus BP currency needed for lots of upgrades.

However, while the gameplay itself is really well-done, it suffers from some glaring design flaws. The game includes light stealth in it, which seems to be incredibly basic and somewhat tacked-on. The camera is a bit finicky due to it constantly automating Raiden’s backside, and the game throws tons of high elevated/flying enemies at you with a character that’s moveset mostly consist of melee attacks, making fights with them frustrating and annoying. But otherwise, Platnium still delivers a fantastic combat system that will definitely encourage players to replay the game for multiple playthroughs.

The basic plot isn’t as difficult to follow as other MGS games but trying to understand it can be massively disorienting, due to the game’s constant references to real-life events and it’s sometimes weird combination of a gritty or absolutely stupid tone. While it can make the game often have pacing issues, for the most part it’s a surprisingly memorable story with memorable characters and hilarious moments often breaking up the often monotone tone of the game.

The presentation for the game is good. The game does a fairly decent mix of playable performance and eye-popping visuals, and the overall aesthetic of the game is pretty good. The music is on a completely other level, with a stellar soundtrack filled with epic boss battle music and insanely ridiculous metal rock. It sounds like something that wouldn’t fit in a Metal Gear game but it surprisingly complements the insanity of this game pretty well.


The PC Port for the game marked Platnium’s first PC Release, and was fairly alright. The caps it’s framerate at a constantly smooth 55-60fps and the visual settings for the game are minimal at best. While you can change the keybinds if you’re playing with a keyboard I highly advise playing with a controller.

In conclusion, Metal Gear Rising is definitely a good romp to play through. Great combat, stellar gameplay mechanics (with some odd design choices mixed in), and a killer soundtrack really nails it in as a very good Metal Gear spinoff.

TL;DR - The well-thought out combat, campy plot and killer soundtrack makes this one of the best MGS spinoffs you can play right now.

Thanagor Doccy
520 products in account

Recommended
7.2 hrs on record
Posted: October 4, 2014
I have a "love and dislike" relationship with Platinum Games. Vanquish is my favorite PG game of all-time. Even though I did not like Bayonetta very much, I loved Vanquish, and the feeling is mutual with Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance.

Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance is an action game at its core, and it should not be mistaken for a straight-up Metal Gear Solid game. Hence, the "Solid" word is not even in the title.

What Metal Gear Rising does right is good, action combat. While it may not have the insane and meticulous combo options as Bayonetta, it does enough in the combat department to warrant some good action.

The visuals are spot on for what a 1080p-ported video game would look like on the PC. There are just enough graphics options there. The max resolution is 1080p. It is quite a feat for Japanese developers in general to get a deecent-to-good port. I'll take it.

My only quam with MGS:R is the awkward camera and field of view. Now, before anyone thinks that it is fine for a game of this genre and nature, I would like to step in the argument and disagree. There are video games like Ninja Gaiden that has a good field of view, the developers designed the game to zoom out a certain distance to give the player a good view of the third-person action that is happening during gameplay. Platinum Games dropped the ball here. Since it is not a claustrophobic video game like Dead Space, there is really no reason to make the field of view and camera zoom set to this restricted setting.

MGS:R is best played with a controller so I hope you have a controller.

The story is somewhat cheesy, but I feel like the Metal Gear Solid series was also cheesy to a certain extent. It is good cheese though. It's suitable for this type of game.

Raiden's voice is rather annoying. He sounds like a whimp. Thank goodness he kicks ass in the game.

What else can I say? Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance is a solid effort from Platinum Games. While it may not match the quality of gameplay as Vanquish and Bayonetta, it is a solid entry for the Metal Gear (Solid) franchise.


Rating: 8.5 out of 10.

28 people found this review helpful 0

Recommended
66.2 hrs on record
Posted: December 9, 2019
Holy mother of jesus christ it's a cyborg chopping other cyborgs and robots in a billion pieces like they're made of cardboard.

This game's premise is so ridiculous but nevertheless extremely fun. It doesn't even matter if you're not terribly interested in metal gear or its lore, (although following the story will definitely improve the experience) you will be entertained regardless.

COMBAT
The combat system is obviously the main appeal for the game. Tight combo based swordplay that will feel familiar for anyone that has played bayonetta, or similar titles.

The game rewards execution of parries, combos and using the signature "blade mode" which allows for viciously cutting your enemies in slow motion and in whichever direction you want, to retrieve their internal spine thingy, in order to heal yourself.

There is a weak and strong hit with your blade or secondary weapon of choice (the secondary takes the role of strong hit), and they can be mixed together to pull off satisfying combos that can even launch enemies into the air and it's just so much fun for the whole family.

The parry system works with the same key as the main weak attack, which may seem weird but you get used to it quickly. A dodge+attack system is also implemented via upgrade a bit deeper into the game, which improves the flow of combat and effectiveness of the defensive abilites at your disposal.

BOSSES
Boss fights can be quite challenging, (especially when playing in hard mode, which I definitely recommend) usually requiring of multiple attempts in order to figure out their patterns, attacks that you can parry etc.

Following usual metal gear fashion, they are uniquely designed and have a bunch of gimmicks of their own. The game also features fights against some giant foes that make you feel like even more of a badass cyborg ninja killing machine, which is really what we all want in the end.

Taking a page from megaman, some of the bosses' weapons can be unlocked an used as secondaries which replace your "strong" attack. They come with their own upgrades and add more depth and variety to the combat. The polearm is long range and has flashy spinning combos, the sai allows to stun enemies and the pincers are hard hitting, but slow and they reward timing and predicting the movements of your enemies.

STORYLINE
The story manages to keep itself interesting amongst the crazy amount of action packed cutscenes, which is surprising, although being set in the metal gear universe helps quite a bit.

There are some ridiculous scenes such as the one where it's simply a joy to watch.

EDIT: after careful consideration I'd like to add that the plot and characters in this game are a gift from god in every conceivable way. For some reason they decided to add existential philosophy and a "subtle" (as subtle as an elephant walking the streets of New Jersey) commentary on the war economy and its ramifications to a game about chopping stuff with a hot knife. Somehow they managed to make the most Kojima-esque storyline in a game which he wasn't even involved in for the most part. You will NOT forget a single line of dialogue in this, mainly since it's been memed to death, but the very reason that it's been memed to death is simply because it's genuinely interesting and compelling but it's also a parody of itself pretty much. Anyway, back to the actual review.

OST
When it comes to soundtrack, it mostly consists of adrenaline pumping electronic+metal/rock mix with hardcore elements. It sets the mood quite well and giving the songs vocals instead of keeping them fully instrumental was a good decision I'd say.
"A Stranger I Remain" is my favourite track out of the bunch but all of them are good

NEGATIVES
The camera can be a bit of a mess sometimes. By default, its sensitivity is quite low to keep up with the action, so you'll need to adjust it. Still, it feels weird, and keeping track of multiple enemies can get hard. Before getting the "dodge" upgrade, parrying is your only defensive option, and it's a bit unintuitive, which may throw off a lot of inexperienced players, leading to struggles in the first fights of the game. Most consumable weapons (grenades, RPGs etc) don't feel too satisfying or useful, so you'll end up using the sword for the most part. Only time I found myself actively using them was for some boss fight where EMP grenades were almost mandatory.

Speaking of bosses, while they are fun and unique in which way you approach each one, they are also subject to difficulty spikes. Some bosses feel really easy (cough mistral cough) while others like the blade wolf are hard as balls.

The game's visuals, while not being bad per se, come from this weird drab and "brown" looking era of games. I understand this is metal gear we're talking about, but they could be a bit more colourful and memorable. The level design especially feels quite empty and boring. The game itself is linear and the only incentive for exploring a bit is the possibility of getting consumable items found in boxes around the level.

Finally, it is a bit short. The extra content from VR missions, DLC and replayability of the main story help to mitigate the problem, but it still leaves you wanting more.

CONCLUSION
The game is just really fun and intense. it's more accesible than other metal gear titles because of the focus on action, but it's also deep enough to be rewarding for more advanced players. If you feel like cutting stuff and looking cool while doing it, this is the game to get.

Recommended
30.4 hrs on record
Posted: April 17, 2021
Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance, the spin-off for the Metal Gear series, made as a lightning-speed slasher twisted with Kojima's favorites: pretty long-winded speeches about fates of the world and poor souls in it, and stealth sequences. In the slasher game, it feels really awkward, even ruins the whole game pace sometimes, but... Then again, it is a damn good slasher game. Enhanced with the somewhat unique ability to cut through so many things on every level. Sadly, I can't really describe that selling point feature well enough. I've read some other descriptions before I played the game, but they were not that much impressive as well. You have to see it, actually. Or, even better, try it for yourself.

However, there's one more typical catch: the camera. You know, I've played all my game through without significant troubles, on the standard camera setting. And then I tried to play it on some other PC, on another account, and gosh, it was a terrible experience, where I couldn't follow the enemies' movements, where the camera was always against me and I was always receiving the blows from the directions which I couldn't see. I've tried to tweak it back with the game's options and partially succeeded. But not completely. So, if you see some praisings for Metal Gear Rising in one review, and then some invectives in the next one, know that they both are somewhat on point.

I'm not the one to sing dithyrambs for Kojima's genius, and I actually disdain all that extreme pathos so typical for Japanese-made games. So I was skipping all those unbelievably childish animations and struggling with yawning during unmissable monologues. But as we speak for the action part... I've enjoyed that experience. Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance is marvelous in that old good ultra-violence, especially when you master the blade mode. Which is not that difficult, but all the way fun (minding the treacherous camera, though).

So, as for markings, let's say 8/10. Skip the boring intermedia overloaded with pathos and let the heads keep rolling!

mask
172 products in account

49 people found this review helpful 0

Recommended
67.3 hrs on record
Posted: September 23, 2014
Metal Gear Rising is part of the Metal Gear Saga, albeit not in the form known to most of us. It is not a stealth game, it is a totally silly yet cool action game; Raiden, the "hero" of Metal Gear Solid 2, is back as the main character

The gameplay is based around cutting and parrying. You have "Weak" attacks and "Strong" attacks, weak attacks are faster and strong attacks are slower, which can leave you quite open; there's parry, the bread and butter of this game, you can use this technique by pressing Forward and Weak Attack at the same time, note: If you parry too early, it wil just block, you need a certain timing to counter. This will take some time to get used to, but stick with it and it will pay off, especially, at higher difficulties like Revengeance. In the Revengeance difficulty, Parry will most likely kill, break all the armor, or do massive damage to enemies. In lower difficulties this is not the case! So keep that in mind.

Moves, weapons, armor, and misc items are unlocked with BP, points you get while playing the game. I'll be honest and say that quite a bunch of the moves will be rarely used, but are not entirely useless. However, you NEED Defensive Offense, this is your dodge move. Like its name says, it is a defense move that does damage! It is available since the first mission, but in my opinion it should be a standard move instead of buyable.

Zandatsu is another unique mechanic to this game, it is activated while using Blade Mode. Blade Mode by itself, it allows Raiden to control the direction of his slashes, this however, drains enery, this is where Zandatsu comes! When in Blade Mode, and enemies have no armor (this is important), you will see a square with a red outline, if it is slashed you will get a prompt, this makes Raiden remove the enemies' cyborg energy units, which will heal you AND replenish your energy. Done well, you will never run out of energy!

This game has a ranked system, which increases replayability, you get certain bonuses if you don't recieve damage, no kills (Cyborgs are the only ones counted as kills, UGs, or rather, robots are not), or stealth (this is really rare though). Certain ranked battles are hidden and are easily missed, those are the blank squares that show up when you finish a mission.

Bosses, are easily the hightlight of this game game, they are fun, badass, hard and come with amazing music. I shall say no more, however, you will know when you play it.

Being a Metal Gear game, it comes with the traditional VR Missions, they are very varied and they WILL take a while to get S rank.

CONS: This game has a rather pitiful camera, so bear with me and stick with it, you will get used to. But certain encounters, due to location, are in rather tight places and it will cause you to rage and wonder why the hell it is like that. TELL ME ABOUT IT! The game is worth your time though. So give it a try, and you might have a really fun time.

Recommended
18.1 hrs on record
Posted: January 17, 2014
Great game for fans of the genre. The storyline and gameplay are both top notch, and neither feel as if one is sacrificing the other. The combat system is really detailed and for someone who is new to the genre i found the game play to be pretty challenging at first but easy to grasp and get better at.


The Good

* Great story line / graphics / game play
* Solid gamepad controls
* Easy to start, hard to master.



Needs Improvement

* Visibility and camera control issues
* Mouse controls have built in acceleration
* FPS is locked at 60fps, does not support higher fps or higher refresh rates (i.e: 120hz+)



Overall Rating

8 / 10

Yodzilla
1,055 products in account
0
33 people found this review helpful
2 people found this review funny 0

Recommended
61.4 hrs on record
Posted: January 31, 2018
Metal Gear Rising:Revengeance is Third Person Perspective Hack'n Slash game made by Platinum games and released by Konami, it is also a spin-off to Metal Gear Solid franchisecreated by Hideo Kojima and Kojima productions. This port was released on Steam in 19 february 2013 (Holy crap, my birthday) with all the DLC from consoles.

Story takes place in four years after Metal Gear Solid 4:Guns of the Patriots, which means 2018. Raiden is a cybernetic ninja working PMC specialised in protection of VIPs, however he fails his mission thanks to group of mercenaries known as Desperado Enforcement LCC. and their commanders, Winds of destruction. With new body and equipment Raiden begins his revenge. Not as complicated as in the main series but at least it is a good excuse to cut everything on our way.
Raiden deserves his nickname, because in combat he is fast like a damn lightning god, aside from fast and heavy attack he can use his zandatsu to slow time and cut enemies to pieces as long as his energy meter is not empty, in half of the game he is able to enter ripper mode much increasing damage, but sucking energy from him. Sometimes we can sneak using carton box but it is not giving you any points towards final rank so just ignore it. The key to win every battle is mastering the parry, if you think you cannot block incoming attack you can always dodge (Game will not tell you about that, press x on keyboard, I do not know how to do this on controller).
Beside of various enemies we must face bosses, which are decent because each one of them is more like examinator than executioner, the first one test our bullet dodging skills, second tries our parrying, third require experience in crowd control etc.). QTE exist but they were limited to finishers, which does not make them more enjoyable.
Every location, boss or encounter has one thing that makes this game special, soundtrack. You will not find even one bad track, each one of them perfectly fits everything and makes you sweep faster and faster.
Between missions we can change our equipment, buy new attacks or upgrades. It is worth noticing that beating the game on several difficulties, completing VR-Training missions (that are much harder) and finding collectibles unlocks big part of content which is wuite rare in this age of DLC. None of these items will make you overpowered though.
Graphics are not something incredible but are good enough for a normal PC port.

I do not get how MGR made without Kojima is liked but Metal Gear Survive not. Anyway, back to the case, 8,8/10 for all those hours of fun.
