Recommended
22.2 hrs on record
Posted: August 1
Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance is my Game of the Year by far. I can't say much about this Xbox 360 port that hasn't already been said, the gameplay is phenomenal (for the most part). The soundtrack is the best of the best, I don't like metal that much but i listen to these songs on a daily basis. The story is a little iffy at times, due to it's simplicity (not always a bad thing). My biggest annoyance with the game is how little the game tells you at the start (I'm looking at you, parrying and zandatsu systems), while the game has tutorials on many of the moves you can do, they are all optional, save for the running, jumping, attacking, parrying, etc. while that system is a small inconvenience at times I actually think it works in the game's favor, finding out how to use a new move effectively gives a feeling that I very seldom come across. The absolute worst part of this game is it's length, it's a 5-8 hour long game depending on how thorough you want to be. While some of the bosses and enemies can seem unfair at times they usually require a different approach to them (looking at the final boss for this one), while on the topic of bosses, this game has some of the most fun and challenging bosses that I've had the (dis)pleasure of fighting in a video game, played on normal and died a minimum of 3 times to most bosses.

HIGHLY recommend to anyone who likes shutting their brain off and slicing up cyborgs while talking about memes. 9.2/10


play this game pls i beg

Posted: August 31, 2015
Woooooooowwwwwww. Buy it.

Just getting the unhelpful review part out of my system early.

Buy this game if you like action.
Buy this game if you like Platinum Games (Minus Legend of Korra)
Buy this game if you like difficult games.
Buy this game if you enjoy fun.

Anyway here's the tiny problems that would scare lesser men from this wonderful thing. You're no lesser man, are you?

- Camera sometimes sucks
- Apparently the game isn't that good at teaching you things, I can't say anything about this since I've had exposure before playing.
- Lock on is useless on more than one target.
- It's short if for some reason you don't replay it.
- Some voice acting is just not really good. (But you won't care.)
- You have no reason to give a damn about the story.
- The first boss is adorable but you have to kill it.
- The hype makes me smell awful.
- If you aren't good at the game then it's going to feel sucky and lame :(

Now here's why you should play it.

+ You have no reason to give a damn about the story.
+ Cutting things is just wonderful fun.
+ The combat is amazing minus rare camera mess ups.
+ Everything goes ♥♥♥♥♥♥♥♥ at the end. It's awesome.

+ Essentially cardio in game form.
+ You can drop kick a robotic gorilla with a machine gun on its arm, then grab it by the leg, slam it on the ground, and cut it 50 times in a few seconds with bullet time. And then you can eat a cyborg's spine to recharge.
+ Just buy the game.

10/10

MGRR is a very creative and bizarre game in a lot of ways. It takes place in a world where firearms and other contemporary weapons have mostly been rendered obsolete in favor of anime style cyborg ninjas and 50 foot tall mechs. Recommended
58.2 hrs on record
Posted: October 21, 2020
Let me start by answering a few basic questions:
1. Does MGR have the mechanical depth of Bayonetta or DMC? No, not even close. The weapons are less versatile, there are less of them and Raiden's abilities aren't as complex as other protagonists in this genre.
2. Does MGR have the complex stealth gameplay of the parent series? No, not even close. What little stealth is here is below Assassin's Creed in terms of depth.
3. Does any of that matter? No, not at all.

This is one of the most unique action games ever made, striking a compelling middle ground between your prestige character action games and more basic hack&slash fare. Combat is fast and frenetic whilst requiring some patience and precision for high level play. If you want to enjoy this game to it's fullest, LEARN THE PARRY MECHANIC: it is barely explained outside of an optional VR mission and without mastering it, you will get slaughtered on higher difficulties.

Unravelling and digesting this games combat system across multiple runs is a joy, and it helps that the game itself has one of the best written (yes I said it), most entertaining short campaigns of the last decade.

Recommended
28.9 hrs on record
Posted: February 13, 2016
Meta Gear Rising is an action hack and slash game in the style of the Devil May Cry Series but in the Metal Gear world. So if you liked DMC you will like MGR.

This game is a pure action game and is nothing like the Metal Gear games which are more stealth oriented games.

You play as Raiden a cyborg enhanced human soldier who fights for a private military firm. The story is set in the future when private military companies are trying to manipulate politics to suite there hidden agenda.

The game is non-stop action with high adrenaline music and epic cut scenes that tell the story. The boss fights are also quiet epic and rewarding when you finally win.
When you advance in the game you receive battle points. With these points you can buy upgrades for your weapons and armour, new battle suits and health and new skills. Hidden in the game you can find upgrades for your health, grenades, ...

A unique skill in this game is the ‘Blade Mode’. When the ‘Blade Mode-bar‘ is full you can activate this. It’s a sort of slow motion sequence when you can cut your opponents in slices – it’s impressive and a big part of the game.

The game is best played with a gamepad. The Xbox 360 or Xbox One controller work flawlessly.

The game can be quiet difficult and frustrating at times – especially the boss fights against the senator.
I nominated the 'Senator' of 'The “Villain Most In Need Of A Hug” Award' in the 2016 Steam Award.

After you finish the game you can access the included 2 DLC stories. In the first story you play Jetstream Sam and in the second you play Bladewolf. Replay ability come from higher difficulty settings, trying to get better battle scores and finding and finishing the more than 50 VR-mission.

The bad :
The game doesn’t support resolutions higher than 1080p. When you want higher resolutions you need to use a ‘hack-program’. I used Flawless Widescreen to play the game in 2560*1080 – 21/9 aspect ratio – this worked without problems but all cut scenes are letterboxed (with black bars).
I believe there is a bug in the game with AMD GPU’s when you activate ‘Blur’ in the graphics options menu. With an AMD GPU you get constant stuttering. With ‘Blur’ deactivated you can play the game at maximum settings.

Conclusion :
I recommend this game.

This game is like a turbo futuristic anime on roids!!! Gave me such a thrill!

Story

You are Raiden, the ninja cyborg from the Metal Gear series, and you work as a private sucurity firm for governments around the word. In the very first chapter of the game you meet up with another private security firm called “desperado” who uses its arsenal to provoque conflicts and wars and generate more demand for private security like the one they offer. This leads to unfolding an evil plot around the government of the United States.

Gameplay

This is probably the best Hack and Slash game I’ve ever played, both because of its story and its smooth gameplay. You really feel like you are some kind of future ninja badazz cyborborg slashing everything in your way with this game. You have an energy bar called “blade mode” that allows you to slice apart almost everything in the game, be it enemies or simply the environment. This is one of the few games that actually give you the sensation of being using a sword as a cutting weapon, instead of as some kind of blunt club, as it feels like in most game. Also, mobility is amazing as you have your ninja run button that makes you run and climb fast through the environment.

Boss Battles

The icing on the cake in this game are the boss battles, man, how amazing they are! Each boss has his unique looks and style and also, before fighting, there is the classic philosophical discussion about “good and evil”, “protecting the weak” and the more the villain boasts as brags about his superiority, the more satisfying it is to slice him apart in the end. BTW: Notice how the final boss has a similar mentality to Donald Trump. Coincidence? I don’t think só…

Overall, this is the best slasher that I have ever played, I just wish it were longer…

I give it 4.8/5.0

RAVIOLI CONNOISSEUR
141 products in account
0
19 people found this review helpful
1 person found this review funny 0

Recommended
54.6 hrs on record
Posted: May 31, 2018
Despite some frustrating flaws. Metal Gear Rising is absolutely worthy of the Metal Gear name and worth your time if you are a Metal Gear fan.

I am not shy to admit Metal Gear is one of my favorite franchises of all time, including all spin offs. There's more to Metal Gear, than just Metal Gear Solid and games directed by the overly revered to, Hideo Kojima.
In this sense Metal Gear Rising feels simultaneously like a fresh experience and a proper continuation of the world after MGS4.
It's not all perfect as some mechanics and areas dont' feel fully finished or fleshed out. Or outright tacked on. In the case of VR missions, they feel poorly designed and can be incredibly frustrating for all the wrong reasons and is the first time I have called it quits on finishing all the content available in a MG game.

I am going with negative points first, but don't misunderstand me. Despite the problems, I LOVE this game. The fighting system has an amusingly large amount of depth for as unconventional as they designed the system to be compared to contemporary character action games.

Port wise, it's a disappointingly mixed bag. So let's start with cons.
__________
[Cons]
The game only offers a fixed set of resolutions limited to a max of 1080p (Not forward thinking damn it!), you can use a 3rd party tool to edit in other resolutions. But 16:9 only, and often it will break certain rendering.
The mouse cursor doesn't auto hide. Requiring you to move it constantly or use an auto hider program.
It has bug that doesn't properly detect your referesh rate. (Itself caused by stupid HDMI EDID standards for video resolutions that dont' have anything to do with computer use and only serve to screw things up ) This doesn't affect me since I have refresh rates less than 60hz removed with an EDID override.


The biggest problem however is performance stability. The game itself performs extremely well and isn't hard to hit 60FPS for general gameplay. When it comes to maintaining that though,even with both Zan options set to low the game still crushes a single CPU core with Zandatsu, causing the framerate to drop catastrophically. 

However most egrigious is the completely broken frame rate limiter/frame pacing.This damn near ruins the experience if it wasn't for the fact that the existing console versions have genuine framerate problems.

The game runs at 60FPS, but the cutscenes are 30FPS FMV files. In itself not a bad issue, the problem is the frame limiter does not pace the 30FPS videos properly. Leading to tons of dropped frames and hitches during playback.

Even more awful is the 60FPS limiter, at first glance the game seems stable with decent frame pacing and no hitches or microstutter. After about 15-30 minutes the limiter starts to break and frame times are all over the place. At first it's just a one off hitch/stutter ever 20-30 seconds. The more time goes on, the more frequent these stutters/hitches become until they are happening every few seconds or more.

The only way to fix it is to close out of the game and restart it. Believe me I tried everything possible short of having a Free Sync or Gsync monitor.

Forcing driver level vsync doesn't fix it.
Disabling vsync or running windowed doesn't fix it.
Using more or less pre-rendered frames doesn't fix it.
Using a 3rd party frame rate limiter to try and clean up the frame time stability works well until the problem starts occuring. (Using a whole number limit or a fractional framerate limit using config tweaks with RTSS).
I even went so far to think that maybe for whatever reason internally the limit is actually expecting an exact 59.94hz output, so what did I do? I used Custom Resolution Utility to modify my display's actual refresh rate to be as close to 59.94hz as possible (As this display is normally set to 60.001hz. And tests confirm these modifications do actually change the refresh rate) This seems to grant a more stable paced experience a bit longer before the hitching kicks in. But no dice.
I also tried the fan made "Force Fix" for people with refresh rates available lower than 60. And all that served to do was break shadow rendering in random scenes.

I have an older CPU , a Core i7 950 overclocked to 4Ghz. Which can account for the Zandatsu problems. But I doubt it is to blame for the frame pacing problems.



A very pooly designed camera system that has you constantly fighting with it to achieve what you want. This is my biggest complaint game mechanic wise. There are so many situations where the camera just does not work, or does something unexpected and since your input works in relation to the current camera view. Will cause you to be unable to do what you want, ruin a no hit situation, ruin a stealth situation as the camera randomly wants to suddenly rotate back to some strange default posistion.
The game seems to have 4 conflicting camera systems, 1 if you don't use the right stick at all the camera attempts to auto rotate in relation to the character movements or physical boundaries within game space. With how the maps are designed and ESPECIALLY the VR missions. This straight up doesn't work and so you reach for the stick to manually move the camera. This is system 2, however it directly competes for control with system 1 and so system 1 starts counter steering the movements from system 2 causing them to fight for control. (When lock on is used it takes the place of system 1 and I dub this system 4)Leading to the majority of the problems, doubly so when you start hitting physical boundaries in game space. Walk to a wall, try to rotate manually to face opposite and system 1 says no, screw that i'm going to attempt to auto-snap to a predetermined angle instead at the same time. Causing you miss or mess up a cruicial input because again, movements and actions are based in relation to camera space.
System 3 are the cinematic angles used during scripted encounters with bosses or bigger UGs. This takes the place of System 1 and partially disables system 2. When system 4 is enabled it works better here than when used during normal gameplay.
Speaking of system 4, the lock on camera is pretty spotty. It's difficult to simply select the target you really want and the game seems to auto assign based on certain values.
Overall, I don't recall the last time I found myself loudly verbally cursing a game's camera than in Metal Gear Rising and is my biggest complaint about the game overall. Nowhere does this feel more valid than in VR missions where the limitations become even more apparent and it makes the VR missions feel tacked on and obvious that a fixed camera in many scenes would have worked better for this game mode specifically. (Which they did do in the side view stages. Just not consistently across all missions.) The Ninja Kill animation in particular can ruin you in VR missions that require it if you need to make a quick camera adjustment but can't because System 2's camera is locked momentarily after the animation finishes.



Situations where a cutscene ends, just to have you really do nothing gameplay wise but to walk forward and trigger another scene. These feel like they should've been just one continuous scene, and in general I wish the cutscenes were slightly longer. Codec conversations are a plenty however and feel right at home.
Cutscenes are disappointingly for the first time in the series offline rendered in-engine video files. And they are only 720p in resolution. Effects quality is a lot higher here and the compression is actually on par with the PS3 version at least. But image quality is still a bit rougher since there is still a ton of aliasing due to them being rendered at 720p.


Review continued through comments.

󠀡󠀡󠀡⁧⁧ZacHsȺshes
871 products in account
0
26 people found this review helpful 0

Recommended
71.8 hrs on record
Posted: January 27, 2014
I could just link you to sounds of sensual moaning, but I think I'd rather use my vocabulary to describe why Metal Gear Rising: Revengence is an astoundingly great game. Yes, I'm using sections, because a simple blurb wouldn't do this masterpiece justice. I should note that I had very little prior experience with the Metal Gear series, having only played about a half of the original Metal Gear Solid.


Premise
You play as Raiden, a cyborg ninja with a very violent and traumatizing past. Part of Maverick Security, a self-titled "private security contractor", you and your agency have spent the past three years protecting a fledgling African nation while it grew into a prosperous society. All that changes when the president of the nation is kidnapped and assassinated by another cyborg, who works for one of your rivals, Desperado LLC. From there, you find out the who, what, and why of the assassination - the misery branches off from there.

Being a cyborg ninja, you have quite a lot of finesse, leaping over buildings and other objects with ease. Of course, no ninja of questionable authenticity would be caught dead without a katana, or rather, a High-Frequency blade. With it, you can cut nearly anything and anyone with ease - mind the other cyborgs with one, though!


Gameplay
The Sword
By now, you can probably tell that Metal Gear Rising's meat and bones is the HF Blade. It's most obvious application is slashing up enemies. There are two modes of attack: light and strong. Light allows Raiden to attack without breaking his run, while heavy, while more damaging, forces Raiden to come to a complete halt. There are many combos to learn and attack styles to perfect, but it never becomes quite as overbearing as a fighting game's controls.

Parrying. Parrying parrying parrying. The most important maneuver in the game. Without it, your enemies will make mince meat of you, especially on higher difficulties. When an enemy glows red, it is time to parry. Press attack + the direction in which the enemy is, and you will successfully parry if you get the timing right. Forgive me for typing the previous two sentences out as though I were writing a textbook, but it is better to learn it now than in-game, hair ripped out and four hours wasted on the first boss.

Blade mode is another crucial element to MGR's swordplay. It can be activated at any time to slice objects or people more accurately, but people are what it's primarily used for. After widdling down an enemies health to a certain degree, you can go into blade mode and perform Zandatsu - a maneuver in which you slice the enemy in half and rip their cyborg guts out, exploding them in your hand to regain health and energy for blade mode. It's as awesome as it sounds.

With these elements combined, the swordplay is extremely smooth and satisfying, when done correctly. Zandatsu is just the cherry on top, the thing that makes everything else worthwhile.

Encounters and Rankings
Encounters (not official nomenclature) are composed of enemies of varying strength and difficulty. Most are boxed in and prohibit the player from progressing through the terrain. Not much else to say about the encounters themselves, but each are ranked from D to S, D being "you suck ♥♥♥♥" and S being "you didn't take any damage and got lots of points". Points are awarded depending on the enemies killed, the number of Zandatsus performed, the damage you took, and the time it took you to beat it. At the end of each chapter of the game, you ranks are tallied up to form a rank for the entire chapter. Those points aren't just for show, either...

Upgrades
Upgrades are what makes getting those points worthwhile. After every checkpoint in the game, you are able to go to the cleverly-titled "Upgrade Screen" and buy upgrades for Raiden. You can give Raiden's sword stat increases, buy unlocked "sub-weapons", increase Raiden's health and Blade Mode battery, and even get different skins for his armor. This system is one of the reasons why Revengence is as replayed as it is, as it allows for upgrades to be carried over to a new game.

Stealth
Although Metal Gear Rising is primarily an action game, there are many segments where stealth is not only an option, but is encouraged. Running up behind an enemy and pressing the action button will activate Ninja Mode - which is a fancy way of saying you can slash enemies silently. The cardboard box is as useful a tool as ever, and there are even smoke grenades to help sneak past enemies. It is also worth noting that sneaking past an area that is set up for an Encounter forgoes the grade you would get for fighting, which can be quite useful for keeping a consistent grade.

Secrets and Unlocks
A lot. Magically turns 5 hours into 40.

Overall
Though it isn't in the title anymore, the gameplay is still SOLID. The swordplay is engaging, the scoring and upgrade systems are rewarding and encourage replayability, and the stealth system feels like a natural extension to the gameplay. The only complaint that I have is that the camera can't keep up with the action sometimes - like it realizes how awesome you're doing and freaks out.

As a side note, I think complaints that the story is only five hours long is misguided, to say the least. This is a game all about skill, improving yourself. As such, you'll want to go for better rankings and for harder difficulties, because you want to see how good you can get. At bare minimum, you'll keep playing for the upgrades and unlocks, which, as previously mention, add a sizable amount of time spent playing. VR missions, small challenge levels, add even more length and challenge. Even if that doesn't tide you over, at least Revengence comes with two DLCs that lengthen the experience by a few hours.


Presentation
The gameplay is spectacular on it's own, but it's how the game presents itself that propels the entire experience to greatness.

Story
Without going into much detail here (partially because of spoilers, partially because of laziness), Metal Gear Rising's story is... wild. And deep. What starts off as a simple mystery turns into a... err... complex mystery, filled with conspiracy and political ideology. Though the game has an air of self-aware cheekiness, it manages to be surprisingly engaging when the plot gets good. At the game's climax, the wackiness and the seriousness combine to create something utterly incredible. Also of note is the boss characters - possibly the coolest portrayal of traditional archetypes I've ever seen.

Sound
You know a soundtrack is good when you actively have to force yourself not to type the lyrics in all caps right this second. Much like the story, it is both over-the-top and yet extremely captivating. The lyrics to the songs are pertinent to the story and characters, with boss theme's reflecting their respective character's personalities and modus operandi. The music that plays during regular encounters is a treat as well, while the stealth music feels calm and controlled. Nu-metal was a surprisingly perfect choice for the feel of Revengence.

Graphics
Honestly, probably the weakest part of the whole package. Most of the environments look extremely drab, sometimes muddy - I didn't know a cloudy day in Denver looked that horrid. Meanwhile, the characters, while well designed, have low texture quality - it's not very noticeable unless seen very close.


Conclusion
Metal Gear Rising: Revengence is a well-thought out, well-crafted game. It might not try to swoon the player with promises of progressive writing *cough* Bioshock Infinite *cough*, but between its fantastic gameplay, high-but-attainable skill ceiling, fun and engaging story, and rocking soundtrack, MGR lives and dies by its dedication to the hardcore. I don't like to flaunt being a gamer, but if you consider yourself to be one, a TRUE one, pick this up without hesitation.

Posted: July 7, 2016
Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance * 8/10

Metal Gear Rising is the last chapter in the Chronological Timeline of the Whole Metal Gear Saga. But even though it shares the story, the settings and the themes with the saga it essentially throws in the dumpster all the stealth mechanics that marked and represented all the other titles in favour of a more rushing hack'n'slash style. Well, to be honest even the story is secondary as it's quite simple and lets the player focus more on the gameplay and the characters' charisma.

4 years after the Patriots incident Raiden finds himself working for Maverick, a Private Military Company, with the task of protecting N.Mani an African country prime minister. Another underground outlaw PMC named Desperado will assault your convoy to kidnap the senator and eventually kill him. You will fight your way to the PMC leader, Jetstream Sam, and as usual you will be defeated, then the real game will start.
Until that moment you will have already seen most of the key elements of this game. As I've already mentioned the game is definitely a Hack & slash game with a particular innovation: Raiden's katana. Your main weapon is capable of completely cutting almost everything, starting from your enemies during blade mode, where time slows down and you can slice your opponents in literally hundreds of pieces while your energy drains during this action. You can't roll away from enemies attacking you (an I HATED this) but the only way you can defend yourself from enemies attacks is a parry system which is assisted on easier difficulties and manually tough on harder difficulties. there are miniboss fights and other fights with HUGE enemies, time action events and extreme action situations that look taken straight from anime such as vertical running sections or jumping on rockets being fired at you. Definitely beyond the limit, but tough and awesome at the same time. Some advanced sections will try to give you a cardboard box and a barrel, both to be used as in a common metal gear, the problem is that besides some forced sections you never feel like it's a good idea to use them as there are always too many enemies and there are rarely blind spots to use for a stealth approach. Exactly the same feeling for the couple of rocket launchers or grenades you can find here and there, I've finished the game and I've used them 2 or 3 times...
As in any respectable Hack & slash game you can improve your character's health and energy, moves, weapon and cyborg armour, though for the first 2 you need to find the relative upgrades hidden in the level. Also you can find VR missions hidden in the levels, which can represent a valid enterteinment expanding the durability of the game, considering that they're not all simple VR missions but some of them include some original mechanics that add that variety to the missions.
Included with the game there are also 2 DLCs unlocked at the end of the main campaign: Jetstream Sam and Wolf prequel Stories which give a little more life to the game, and I advice to play both of them because even if they're short they're still pretty good. There are some tough VR missions hidden there as well (not reachable through the main VR menu).
The game is developed with the Platinum Engine (not Fox Engine), and even though it doesn't make any particular miracle it does its job.
The soundtrack is really tough and badass as it follows and incites the player in the toughest and most intense fight sections especially Boss Fights.


+++PROs+++
GAMEPLAY. Even though a Metal Gear fan could see the total change of gameplay as a trauma, it really is great and fun, a very tough challenge, especially the final Boss and considering how Raiden has been portrayed in MGS4 I personally consider this change of direction and gameplay perfectly understandable.
SOUNDTRACK. Since this chater is a frantic Hack & Slash a badass soundtrack is a MUST. So, what can I say... Check![/] CHARACTERS. I noticed a nice and deep portray of some characters, say Raiden, Jetstream Sam, Wolf and The "final boss", just to mention some, without spoilers.
EXTREME. Considering the legacy and the previous chapters, what is to be seen in this title is extreme: vertical runs and jumping on missiles are the two smallest and least spoilerous examples I can come up with... Yet I Really appreciated all of this, the frenzy of the normal gameplay mixed with these extreme time action events and tough boss fights, and all shown with a great direction worth of Kojima's blessing.
---CONs---
FIGHT STYLE. For a frenzy Hack & Slash game like this being deprived of the ability of dodging attacks in favour of a tough parry system can be a tough challenge but I honestly believe it simply kills the action as you have to wait a long cooldown tie before you can attack and most of times you are forced to parry a sequence of attacks, not just an attack. Not to mention the fact that some attacks can't be parried and you don't have the ability to dodge...
FAILED STEALTH MECHANICS. This game is part of Metal Gear Legacy, yet the developers chose to take the H&S direction, which is fine, considering the character and all the rest. Then Why in the hell try to put just a fistful of forced stealth sections if the only way you can run them is just with boxes or drum cans. You can't crouch, nor crawl, nor get against walls or other props to stay hidden, you can't make noise to distract enemies unless you sprint close to them. No, Stealth as made in this title is quite pointless.
CAMERA. I didn't find myself too comfortable with the camera and control settings. strafing left or right results in turning the camera as well. The camera is slightly left sided, can't be changed and in few times I find it being too close to Raiden. When you want to take a good look at the situation from an observation point or when hiding in the carboard/barrel if you move the camera and leave it still for a second and a half it will instantly turn back... So you essentially can't observe anything taking your time and all... And last and least important the camera look seems quite "uninterpolated"... as if you want to turn left or right a very little bit the camera skips to the next angle instead of sliding smoothly from A to B... I don't know how to explain but it is more evident when you move slightly or even more while you're on codec.

I played this game on this machine:
Intel Core i7-4970
16Gb RAM DDR3
GeForce GTX 660
Windows 10 Professional x64

Metal Gear Rising: Revengance, the game that made up a word just to sound cool. Well, this game does a lot more than sounding cool, it just straight up is. Every battle is epic, especially the boss battles.

There isn't a whole lot to say except the combat is simple but very enjoyable. Platinum is great at making games with incredibly fun combat, just look at Bayonetta. And every boss fight is unique and interesting, and never feels like boss mechanics are reapeating.

Very annoying, and I did have one instance where the camera wouldn't let me see a damn thing and it caused me to die.

Despite this Metal Gear Rising has a very strong combat system with some pretty cool upgrades and different weapons to make combat varied, and the game doesn't outstay its welcome. It took me about 8 hours to beat the main story. Very much worth the buy, just be warned if you don't like cheesy stories, it'll make you roll your eyes.

-Bonus missions to do when your done with the story

Cons:
-Story is dumb

-Shoe-horning in stealth because its metal gear.

Posted: January 18, 2014
Before I get started with the review, I must inform everyone that I played with a controller and not the keyboard and mouse. Some people have had trouble using a keyboard and mouse with the game while others have said that it's better than using a controller. If you do not have a controller then I suggest that you check out other reviews and see if it has good keyboard/mouse support. I'm using what is essentially an Xbox 360 controller. This review will only encompass the main game and not the DLC. I will do my best to not spoil any of the story.

The first thing I'd like to talk about is the interface. Metal Gear Rising's menus aren't what I'd call perfect but they're functional. One of the biggest issues that I've found with the main menu happens to be pretty minor; you can't quit the game without loading your save file first. It's a negligible issue to me but I see it brought up in the Steam forums quite a bit so some people might consider it a bigger issue.

Main Menu and Options Menu:

YouTube™ Video:  
Views: 0


The item menu could stand to be improved but it's likely that you'll never use it in combat anyways. It pauses the game when you press left or right on the directional pad and allows you to pick which weapons you want. When you're being attacked or in the middle of an attack animation then it will seem unresponsive.

The heads up display has a lot of information being shown. Whether or not this is a good thing depends on how much hand-holding you want. It at least keeps itself out of the way during battles and doesn't cover up the entire screen.

Heads Up Display Screenshot:
http://i.imgur.com/BNA1c5L.jpg

User Interface and Heads Up Display:

YouTube™ Video:  
Views: 0


The gameplay is a bit more than just hacking and slashing your way through enemies. It requires accurate timing and precise aim with your sword while under time constraints. Battles are drastically different from the previous entries to the Metal Gear franchise. Stealth is now harder to pull off and there is more emphasis on the action.

You can tell that the boss battles will be over-the-top once you see the first boss. They put you up against a modified Metal Gear Ray in the first few minutes of gameplay. From slicing the armor off to even throwing the Metal Gear, it's clear that Raiden is a lot stronger than he was in previous games. Metal Gear Rising seeks to make you feel like a super-human and I feel like it succeeds in doing so.

Metal Gear Ray battle from the Xbox 360 version:

YouTube™ Video: Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance Metal Gear Ray Boss Battle 
Views: 178,841
See Raiden fight in a sombrero http://bit.ly/11T63Hs Watch Raiden rip a Ray to pieces in this lengthy boss battle from the beginning of Revengeance.


The bosses are unique in Metal Gear Rising. Every single boss has its own way to beat it and even their own theme songs. I feel like this is where Metal Gear Rising shines the most; the boss battles. While the regular enemies put up a bit of a fight, they're mainly just fodder for your blade even on the highest difficulty settings.

The contrasting difficulty from regular enemies to bosses might seem a bit unbalanced, especially when you go up against the final boss which is probably one of the hardest bosses in any game that I have played. I was pleasantly surprised when I actually lost against a final boss. From health regeneration to a larger pool of health and insanely powerful moves that you can only dodge, Platinum Games knows what they're doing to make a boss feel difficult rather than just tedious like so many final bosses in other games.

If it weren't for the amazing music, I probably would have had a harder time against the final boss. That brings me to my next point: the soundtrack. Metal Gear Rising's soundtrack might seem a bit strange for a video game but it definitely suits the gameplay. Each song is different and the lyrics suit the boss that they're made for. The boss battles with their amazing songs are the main reason why I'd consider replaying the game over and over.

One of my favorite boss battle themes(Mistral):
http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=cLvgvsI5jAg

The story is one of the only parts of the game that doesn't really shine. You're a cyborg who has to kill terrorists and that's as much as you need to know in order to justify your character cutting people into tiny bits. The story only briefly references the events of Metal Gear Solid 2 and 4 so it's good even if you haven't played any other Metal Gear games. There are only around two hours of cut-scenes this time which is less than other Metal Gear games; to put this into perspective, Metal Gear Solid 2-4 each had five hours of cut-scenes while the original Metal Gear Solid had over three.

Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance is one of the best action titles of 2013 and I'm glad that Platinum Games ported it to the PC. I feel like they did a good job on the PC port besides a few technical issues that they can easily fix in a patch. There were no noticeable bugs when I played through the game and I feel like it was a polished game.

The PC port is locked to 60 FPS and the resolution can only go as high as 1920x1080. If you're using HDMI then you may run into the same bug as I did where the game switches to interlaced mode by default in 1920x1080. The solution to fixing this problem is to run the game in windowed mode and then using the Windowed Borderless Gaming tool.

Windowed Borderless Gaming tool:
http://forums.steampowered.com/forums/showthread.php?t=2675769

Overall, I feel like this game is worth buying if you're a fan of action games. The game looks much better than it did on the PS3 and 360 due to the increased resolution, frame-rate, anti-aliasing, and texture filtering. If you haven't played this game before then I recommend buying it on the PC if your specs are good enough. It's easily one of the best action games I've played so far.

Recommended
17.7 hrs on record
Posted: January 10, 2014
The PC port of this game is a good one. You've got AA/AF options, plus low/medium/high settings for shadows, how long debris stays, and how many pieces you can cut things into. On my 660Ti, I could run at 1920 x 1080 with MSAA x 2, AF x 16, and everything on high and it holds at 60 FPS with no Vsync tearing whatsoever.

As for the game itself? This was my pick for best game of 2013. It's a Bayonetta/Devil May Cry style action title with stylish choreography (and it's not just limited to the cutscenes; you can and will be doing this stuff yourself) combined with the characterization and dialogue of a traditional Metal Gear title. And there's quite a lot of that, too: if you voluntarily listen to all of the codec conversations and don't just skip the cutscenes, this game is about as long as a "normal" Metal Gear Solid game. Anyone saying "it's short!" is neglecting to point this out, as most of the codec dialogues are optional.

Stealth exists for sections but is actively discouraged. In true Platinum Games fashion, the most critical and fundamental of gameplay mechanics is left under-explained. In this case, that's how to properly parry and dodge (you'll actually have to purchase aerial parrying and the dodge as upgrades, though they are inexpensive and among the first upgrades available). As with most Platinum games, you can go through much of the game without quite "getting" how they work, but once you've got it down your effectiveness will skyrocket. Hint: you have to move the stick FROM NEUTRAL towards the direction of the attack before hitting X.

Platinum Games are about "mastery" more than just "completion." You don't simply beat this game and conclude "well, I've beaten it, now onto the next game" like we do for most action titles. To do so would be missing out on a lot of what is offered. Here, you're graded on each encounter, and to get every encounter per level you'll want to backtrack and intentionally get spotted so as to trigger more fights. Doing better means more points to spend on character and weapon upgrades. You'll get several weapons each with several moves and their own applications. Feel free to use whatever you feel like. Replay past levels using the weapons you got from later stages. Then try out the VR challenges and higher difficulties. And now you can choose to skip straight to the boss fights upon completion (all Metal Gear games should have this).

This is the sort of game where there are multiple difficulties above Hard. The sort of game that's meant to be PLAYED rather than watched in a video playthrough in order to truly experience it. I beat it on PS3 last year, and now I feel like doing it all over again on PC. Here's hoping Metal Gear Solid 5 comes out on Steam too!

This is NOT Metal Gear Solid. And that is OKAY.

Posted: June 28, 2020
METAL GEAR RISING: REVENGEANCE

A hack and slash game with well deserved Overwhelmingly Positive reviews. another great game by Kojima Productions and PlatinumGames. METAL GEAR RISING: REVENGEANCE takes the renowned METAL GEAR franchise into a new arc and gives the game some new features and combat machines. Released for PlayStation 3, Xbox 360, and Microsoft Windows this game received a well-deserved welcome by all.


METAL GEAR RISING: REVENGEANCE 
A Screenshot of METAL GEAR RISING: REVENGEANCE
By: BiteMexD


Story

METAL GEAR RISING: REVENGEANCE takes place four years after the events of Metal Gear Solid 4: Guns of the Patriots. Four years after the events of the Guns of the Patriots Incident, [b1] Raiden [/b1] ( our protagonist ) has been contracted by a private military company (PMC) Maverick Security Consulting, Inc for VIP protection, military training, and other duties.

The game starts off by showing Radien riding with a VIP who he is tasked with protecting. Suddenly they get ambushed and attacked by cyborgs. Led by the cyborg Samuel Rodrigues. During the attempt of trying to rescue the VIP Radien is confronted by the cyborg and defeated. Rescued and reconstructed by his PMC, Raiden starts his journey of vengeance.
his search for Samuel Rodrigues and the company he's working for, Desperado Enforcement LLC.

Gameplay

Being a great Hack and Slash game, the game focuses majorly on combat. and I must say the combat mechanics in this game is very enjoyable and addictive. once you find a combo you like you will be intrigued into using that one only ( or maybe it's just me ). The game starts by lets you some few combats moves than later lets you unlocked other farther down the road. Jumping and running feels very satisfying.
Running headfirst dodging enemies attacks and hacking them to the ground done well. Boss fighters are enjoyable and very well done, I wish there were some more bosses to hack down.


METAL GEAR RISING: REVENGEANCE 
A Screenshot of METAL GEAR RISING: REVENGEANCE
By: BiteMexD


Pro's

Fast, stylish, and technical swordplay.
Decent Story.
Good music.
Well done Bosses.
Decent sense of progression.
Unique gameplay.
Unique game design.
Well made Raiden's abilities.
Decent amount of upgrades and unlocks.
Blade Mode felt smart then expected.
Visuals are well made for that time.
Runs very well on low-end hardware.

Con's

Regular gameplay interruptions.
Some in-game camera issues and unenjoyable camera movements.
Parrying was tedious to learn.
Very Short story.
Raiden's "Jack the Ripper" voice was poorly done.
The Final boss is annoying and not enjoyable.
Lack of character development.
Environment poorly done.


METAL GEAR RISING: REVENGEANCE 
A Screenshot of METAL GEAR RISING: REVENGEANCE
By: BiteMexD


Summary
METAL GEAR RISING: REVENGEANCE is still worth putting your time into.
The pros outweigh the cons. and the cons are minor.
so much to do and see.
I highly recommend it. if you haven't played METAL GEAR RISING: REVENGEANCE yet.
Worth every last penny ( on sale ).
Best wishes, happy Gaming...

BiteMexD
1,331 products in account
5
19 people found this review helpful 0

Recommended
106.2 hrs on record
Posted: April 30, 2014
I could write a novel on how much I enjoy MGR: R.

But I'll keep it short.

The game is a really intuitive game, with a unique and rewarding combat system. The parry is extremely satisfying when you pull off a perfect parry, or block many hits in quick succession. The offensive-defensive, the game's dodge move, also grants a high skill ceiling, with a few frames of invulnerability enabling you to dodge most everything that can't be parried. Mashing the attack button grants an infinite combo, though there's not any hit stun from flaling wildly for most enemies. As Raiden, you are quite literally lightning incarnate. Raiden's not supposed to tank damage, instead you have to block, parry and dodge things.

The boss rush mode in the PC port is a very welcome addition. All of the boss fights in the game are challenging and the variety of them is great. Armstrong's bossfight is nothing like Khamsin's. There's alot of content just in them.

One of the other unique parts of the game, and my personal favorite aspect of it, the OST is very, very good. It's an eccentric mix of electronic-house style music with a dash of contemporary rock and power metal. The soundtrack's vocals kick in at just the right moment in the game's action to give the music a very emotional and exciting complement to the on screen events.

Storywise, the game is still a Metal Gear game. A cyborg ninja and robot dog team up to try and end modern war as a business. Raiden's character arc here is really cool. It echoes MGS2 with Raiden coming to grips with himself, instead of the identity he presents himself as. It's tongue and cheek and over the top at times, but this is nothing new for the series.

The Keyboard and mouse controls are not bad, but you'll want a controller.


There are a few flaws in the game, though. The game's short. (around six to seven hours your first time through.) and the camera messes up frequently. Ninja run is also pretty buggy, you'll die unfairly to messed up pathing a few times through. The DLC, thankfully included for free in the PC port, is not the best. Jetstream Sam's DLC is interesting, but ends too soon, not really giving you an opportunity to use your newfound (though limited) skillset for very long. Bladewolf's DLC is stealth based, but is also very short and re-uses almost all of it's assets from the base game.


Overall I'd say MGR:R is a solid 9.5/10.

GRAPHICS - ★ ★ ★ ★ ☆
From a technical point of view this game feels a bit older. Also there are some minor Bugs. But the very unique Artstyle with Japanese, Cyperpunk and Metal Influence makes this a Joy for the Eye. Also the Cutscenes are over the top with very memorable scenes!

MUSIC - ★ ★ ★ ★ ★
Metal meets Future/Industrial Elements. Also very unique - I think you will hate or love this Soundtrack there will be no between. I LOVED IT!

STORY - ★ ★ ★ ★ ★
Cyborg Ninjas talking about Philosophie while ripping their Limps off. Very Unique and well written Story. Gets very crazy and funny sometimes but surely is something fresh and entertaining.

GAMEPLAY - ★ ★ ★ ★ ☆
Classic God of War with an Sword Element where you can cut Limps of with precise strokes. The Camera is clunky something and you'll need sometime to get a feeling for blocking. Beside that it's an gorgeous Hack'N'Slay!

WORTH BUYING - ★ ★ ★ ★ ★
If you like crazy, brutal and unique Storys or you're a Fan of Devil May Cry or God Of War you should buy this one! It's for sure one of sastisfying games I played in this year!

LENGTH : 7 Hour Story

BUGS : Minor

PRICE : Got it for 3€

DIFFICULTY : Medium-Hard

FINAL:

89 / 100

thatwriterguy
574 products in account
0
34 people found this review helpful 0

Recommended
96.5 hrs on record
Posted: January 14, 2014
RULES OF NATURE
Too few are the games available that offer a chance at sliding along the tail of an enormous mechanical robot atop a high-frequency katana screaming 'RULES OF NATURE' at the top of your lungs. Fewer still are those ported to Steam from console platforms with nary a game-breaking issue in sight. And yet, Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance (MGR:R), first launched on Xbox 360 and PS3 globally during the final weeks of February 2013 is one that has done exactly that.

On January 9th, 2014, the Platinum-Konami lovechild launched near-flawlessly on Steam at a massively reduced price (somewhere in the vicinity of twenty bucks, dependant on your territory and time of purchase) including all 3 DLC sets alongside a host of new graphical options including resolution up to 1080p, 60FPS, gamepad support, anti-aliasing, texture filtering and even the ability to adjust 'ZANGEKI' — the amount of cuts allowed on an object, potentially preventing game crashes or frame rate drops on less capable systems.

I've even read reports on Steam of users testing their system on Can I Run It, with a negative result, that could then, on low settings, play without concern. Impressive, to say the least. But not perfect.

NOT PERFECT?
It's close to perfect, but it's not entirely perfect. For instance, increasing the original FPS to 60FPS is incredible for most gamers, as is the increase in resolution to 1920x1080. Limiting it to 60FPS and 1920x1080, however, is borderline unforgiveable. When moving a title to a new platform, it's important to consider the users of said platform. In the case of PC, 60FPS and 1080p is, for many users, not even playable.

To add insult to injury, there's no Windowed Fullscreen setting forcing many players (and especially Twitch broadcasters like myself) to play windowed to avoid resolution or refresh rate issues. Moreover, there's no V-Sync option, so even if while playing Fullscreen yourself, those watching your broadcast would be forced into an unstable framerate with choppy visuals — something I could only fix by playing windowed.

Even worse still are the cutscenes, which are still limited to 30FPS. Again, this is unlikely to cause an issue for most players, but for some, like myself broadcasting at 60FPS, this means insane screen-tearing and an unpleasant visual experience.

I've been doing some research to determine where these issues are coming from (as, for all intents and purposes my talents lie in playing and critiquing games, not fixing them) and it would appear that the refresh rate not adapting to that of the monitor being used is the underlying cause. Playing in Windowed Mode is the current best fix, though there's a public outcry on Steam requesting a true fix, alongside the addition of V-Sync, WF mode and 120FPS. Here's hoping we get one soon - which is looking likely, as the first patch, to correct the unintended 'always online' function, has already been deployed.

ANYTHING ELSE I SHOULD KNOW?
I found a great post in the Steam forums by Souzooka that details a bunch of issues I haven't experienced myself, but appear common among the community. Here're the highlights:

Players opting to play with a Keyboard and Mouse (presumably because they don't own a compatible gamepad - it's a console game port, people: use a f***ing gamepad) have run into several issues, including the inability to map key bindings to mouse buttons and 'switch lock-on target', alongside a potentially game-breaking issue with aiming the mounted turret in Chapter 4.

Several users have reported game crashes when failing to read the 'ntdll.dll' file. This appears to happen with users that have no C:/ directory. Others have reported crashes when changing resolution (a difficult task, I might add, as changing any of the graphical settings in MGR:R on PC happens immediately, without the traditional 'Apply Settings' option, meaning you'll need to experience the glory of every ♥♥♥♥♥♥ resolution on the way to 1920x1080 before reaching it, and the same for all other options).

Even more worrying are the reports that many users cannot complete the final boss encounter due to an inability to activate the Quick-Time Event (QTE) associated with it, and too, that many cannot save their game. The latter has been linked to Windows 8.1 users who do not have permission to write to their disk, but is unconfirmed.

If you're experiencing any issues yourself, I recommend checking out Souzooka's post here ; there's plenty of good information, and many fixes for strange occurrences.

MGR vs. MGS
That concludes the PC version of this review, and with MGR:R having been available for almost a year I won't be providing a full review on the game mechanics here — that said, I do want to share my perspective on the inception of this title, for those of you that haven't yet picked it up, and aren't sure if you should.

Which is to say, I want to clarify something: this is not a Metal Gear Solid game. I've come across far too many comparisons between MGR:R and MGS this past year and I'd like to beat that nail on the head right now.

MGR:R was developed by Platinum Games, the team that brought you Vanquish and Bayonetta, both high-octane, adrenaline-fuelled action games demanding quick reflexes and an almost insane level of perseverance. The characters, world and story were provided by Konami, and Hideo Kojima himself, creator of the tactical espionage Metal Gear and Metal Gear Solid franchises on the NES and PlayStation 1-3 (and some off-shoot PSP titles no one cares about).

MGS SPOILER ALERT
It's the answer to a question that Konami have been trying to answer for years: what's it like to play as a Cyborg Ninja? In Metal Gear we were introduced to Frank Jaeger, AKA Null, AKA Grey Fox, AKA The Cyborg Ninja. In Metal Gear Solid, we saw Jaeger in action like we'd never imagined, slicing enemies into pieces with the flick of his wrist and providing some of our fondest memories in gaming history. In Metal Gear Solid 2: Sons of Liberty we were introduced to Jack, AKA Raiden, a tactical operative similar in style (but not personality) to MGS protagonist, Solid Snake. During the course of Metal Gear history, Raiden was transformed into the Cyborg Raiden we saw in Metal Gear Solid 4: Sons of the Patriots.

Having been transformed from stealth operative to cyborg ninja, Raiden no longer fit as a playable character in MGS (as anyone who has played MGS2 will understand all too well), and given the engine capabilities of MGS presumably never would again. Unless, of course, one of the most notably epic action game developers on the planet teamed up with Konami to make a game specifically suited to that characters' new style, pace and abilities. Then, y'know, it'd be awesome.

It's understandable that many people went into MGR:R expecting MGS — after all, both titles have at least 2 of the same words — but it's not forgivable. You've got the Internet now, people, and me, and a million others like me. Do your f***ing research before you touch the keyboard to whine about how MGR:R is nothing like MGS - when, obviously, if it was like MGS, it would be f***ing MGS, not MGR:R.

WE'RE OUT OF TIME
Steam has a character limit on reviews, so I can't offer the remainder of it here. If you'd like to read the full review Corsual click this link to be redirected. [www.corsual.com]

Recommended
93.2 hrs on record
Posted: February 25, 2014
I was ready to hate this game, but Platinum did all the right things with it. The tone is a perfect match for the game, and within that tone the story still manages to take the piss out of American Exceptionalism and various other absurdities and platitudes. This is a less philosophical game than general entries in the Metal Gear Solid series, and takes the philosophy of the series less seriously, joking with it in many cases. This is appropriate, as Metal Gear Solid generally overreaches when it tries to do real philosophy anyway. In place of this, we get to explore the motivations and character of Raiden in a game that greatly expands his personal story arc.

As for the gameplay, I found it very good. Much is based on memorization though. The camera can sabotage you at times, which is obnoxious. Also, play it with a 360 controller. Seriously, find a USB 360 controller online and get one, playing this with keyboard and mouse is a dumb idea. Replayability appeal is limited to the appeal of the hack and slash gameplay and to any perfectionist tendencies a player might have, either towards this gameplay or toward the achievements in the game. I expect to put about 40-50 hours into it and probably never touch it after that.
 

Alephwyr
371 products in account
0
20 people found this review helpful 0

Recommended
1.6 hrs on record
Posted: April 2, 2017
This is my favorite brawler from the 360/PS3 generation, and it's one of the best games Platinum has made. Period.

Platinum is known for satisfying and stylish combat, crazy bosses, and balls to the walls concepts. Everyone agrees that their brawlers are the best in the business. But to me, they were still held back, not quite there. Their magnum opus brawler, Bayonetta, was filled with large, empty, and uninteresting levels. It lacked control in terms of immersion (IE, the plot, the setting, the world) and let the gimmicks run wild. Too much filler.

But MGR is different, a fantastic display of Platinum's talents reigned in and controlled. Bayonetta gives you a whole 10min stage devoted to riding a rocket into the city, completely useless padding and a way for the developer to pay homage to Space Harrier. But MGR is much more controlled, and much more demanding with these "gimmicks." They feel spectacular, cool for the moment, yet easily discarded for that next set piece, that next spectacle... as if all that unique assets, programming, was no big deal. The fights jump from set piece to set piece, but in a way that seemed organic and entirely fit the battle that you were already dealing with. Not seamless, (ie, Shadow of the Colossus), but close enough that I could ignore the stitching.

The camera is closer to Raiden when compared to Bayonetta, especially in combat. Not the easiest thing in the world when you are sliding, flipping, and slicing spines in half with enemies and protagonists that are as mobile as the ones in here. But somehow, it never felt bad enough for me to throw my controller into the wall. Perhaps it was a necessity for the Zandatsu mode, a mode that lets you cut anything as if you were wielding a sword lightsaber high frequency blade, but I am glad they were pushing for this "zoomed in" combat. You felt more connected to the character. The cuts feel more visceral, the antagonists more awesome. One of the bosses flips you and the camera flips upside down with Raiden. Cool.

The closer the connection, the more demanding the illusion. And this is where the magic starts to break down. The cuts with "Zandatsu mode" never feel gory enough, and the "cutscenes" oftentimes broke the magic of the fight. I played hard mode from the get go and taking a punch was like getting hammered into your skull. But in the cutscene, I see Raiden getting pummeled and coming back as if barely anything happened. It's a jarring disconnect when you see that happen. Perhaps it gels better when it’s in normal mode… but I love the game too much in hard…

And yet, if you can look past these faults, this is genuinely one of the best brawlers of the last generation. It has a great track integrated well into the game. Fights so spectacular that you wish you could relive it over and over again. And antagonists that were properly unique, cool, and memorable. Just the right amount of discussion of self, identity, nationhood, morality for a game branded with the Metal Gear name. Very little stealth element, but let’s be honest, that could have never happened under Platinum’s development.

This is where I felt Platinum was headed. A great honing of their craft to really push the boundaries and the limits of third person brawlers. But taking a quick look at their body of work now... well, I hope they can keep the lights on for long enough for another great gamble. I will be waiting.
